O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have completed this book for you, dear son, which is the summary of medical knowledge together with its completion, and have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is foreign to all things everywhere, the science is destroyed and decayed, and there remains nothing of it that the hands have not changed, except for the small descriptions in books from the ancients.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off and learning is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It appears that I will vivify it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the shapes of iron cauteries, and the other instruments of work accompanied by the statement of their declaration and preparation, as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hand are found in our time, the art of medicine has become extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who engages in this should be trained in the science of anatomy as Galen says, to such a degree that he knows the judgment of limbs, and their forms and joints and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, tendons, ligaments, and the number of muscles, and the demenement and movement of veins and arteries, and the direction of their outlets.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore, Hippocrates says that the hand with the thumb is much, and with work is little; and the same applies in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the beginning of this book, we say to those who are not learned in the matters previously mentioned that they beware lest they choose incorrectly and operate on men; thus I have often seen more of those who engage themselves in this science and abandon their knowledge and sense of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who opened one abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries in the neck; thus so much blood flowed out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And another man who removed an arrow from a man's side, and the arrow was large; he carried with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had been called to treat it before, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the arrow, and knew well that if it were not cut off, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And another man took care of one duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was an injury; and the ignorant healers bound the break over the wound with strong sutures, and left no skin at the wound, and let it be in this state; and he commanded that it should not be dislocated; and it remained thus until the leg swelled up completely and the toes came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come untie the leg; and when I dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every corruption of a limb was already confirmed and could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop moving through the limb until all the limb was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another mirror that collapsed and then swelled due to the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a cancer, when it is pure of melancholic humour, should not be touched with iron unless it can completely remove what is corrupt in it.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, operations where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	It is necessary that you take care of it so that the foolish man cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Take arms in your case, and treat your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave those diseases that are full of great suffering; and remove your weapons from what causes doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can depart from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen warns in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of bad disease, lest you be called foolish fool."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have organized this treatise according to .iii. chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and against cauterization with medicine for ague, and this chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; and the forms of instruments, and the ironwork of cautery, and everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about ventouse and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you the quality and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the humors and their harm is a long and subtle science and secret responses; and many wise men spoke about it and agreed with it; but they did not give us enough words, for I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all constitutions where there is matter, whether it be two constitutions: namely hot and wet constitution or dry and wet constitution.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry constitution together with matter, some have spoken and said that the fire cautery is great help; and others have said the opposite: that the cautery does not benefit in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure hot diseases by heat or dryness; and he who said otherwise that cautery provides great help for hot and dry disease in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you comprehend the body of man and his heat to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere except by those who have tried it and know through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of the complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their occurrences and the time span; we are not afraid of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the people gathered together and agreed to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cautery with fire is one of the secrets of healing and has more goodness than cautery from burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not harm any other part except the one being heated.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines spread from one member to another by spreading, and bring diseases of great suffering to the sick member, and may kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire due to its high temperature and the goodness of its substance does not do anything if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	I have found this through experiment and the long service and study that I have put into my art, and it was in line with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself from the length of speech, as I do not wish to deprive you of the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it subdues diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says in demonstration; accept this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be done and chose their companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is beneficial in all times, because the harmful events occurring are suppressed by the aid of cautery; and similarly if cauteries are necessary for pain relief, it cannot wait until a greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think so ever, dear child, as the foolish mind does; for a disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say it this way; but it is not as they think, because cauteries are nothing more than medicine that changes the complexion, dries the humors causing pain, and works faster than other medicines due to its power and its virtue.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease itself and its power; and superfluities gather in him through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as in the case of cauteries for pain, and similar cases, and that pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand at all why cauteries are called the rear of medicine; but they do not believe that cauteries have any value after medicine; however, their intentions are false; and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cauteries are the rear of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are more effective than iron ones, but they did not say this without reason, due to the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; they also said that the lees of the cautery do not cause inflammation, but this is not true as I have proven, and I have found it to be true for some men; and cauteries made of gold are more effective than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, when you heat something with gold, you do not know when it is hot due to the color of the gold, and it can suddenly cool down, or if heated too much, it makes fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery which we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Moreover, I have ordered this chapter from the head to the feet, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	hot olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for coldness and moistness on the brain, and in it there are two ways that one does this due to a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and due to many dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and likewise for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient is purged with a soluble medicine cleansing the head for three or four nuis (days) according to what the virtues and age and accustomance of the patient can tolerate; and then heat is applied to the back of the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make the patient sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands on a soft surface; afterward, place the root of your palm on the root of its neck between its two eyes; and where the elbows will come, it will bleed thereafter, then heat the cautery called "olivare", as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place the hot cautery on the spot marked with ink, and draw it along while pulling and twisting your finger; then remove your finger immediately, and watch the spot to see if you can see a small bone; if you cannot see it, repeat the cautery process until you do as I have told you; afterward, take one pinch of wax, wrap it in soft cotton, and put it on the spot, and leave it for three days; afterwards, put soft butter on top; and leave it until the burn is healed; after that, treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when the wound stays open longer, it purges more; and for this reason, if necessary, assist with leeches.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said that one should let the cautery rest for so long that part of the bone is burned, and then heal the burnt bone part.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other said that the cautery should be left for so long, and pushed down with such force as to break the bone as wide as .i. vertoil (approximately 2 fingers) because the humors flow out; then the wound must be left open for a long time, afterwards it must be healed and soothed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for some men with fear; and it seems to me that I should let them be; because the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other limbs; and also when the head of the sick person is weak by nature, the first appearance of cautery seems more healing and beneficial to me, and from this method I work in such a way that it brings salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there comes chronic and lasting pain in the head, the patient should use warm herbs and pills called "cochie," as well as cleansing of the head, oils, and plasters; and if they perform cautery on it, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	If the patient's headache is strong, be careful that it is not too cold; then cauterize under that cautery a little bit as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing cautery on each horn of the head as we have said before, and perform one cautery called "vasselz"; it is a little cauterizer in which ventouses are placed; align your hand so you cannot see the bone: the patient feels more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about that later; and the cauteries on the horns should be finer than those with which one cauterizes the midline of the head, and this is the shape:
dou cautere dou chief	fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes in a part of the head and the disease spreads to the oil (brain), and the head is purged with diverse medicines, and other treatments have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and yet it does not help; then cauteries are made according to two ways, that is, with hot medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with hot medicine is that you take a hot iron and remove the bark from it, and then place one piece of this heated iron on each side of the painful area, so that you can place the hot iron under the skin; and when it is placed in this way, keep the iron under the skin and leave it for twelve hours; then release the iron and treat the wound fiercely and let the wound heal for two or three days; then cover it with linen dipped in butter so that it can be applied again.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment until it heals; and if you see that someone uses some medicines burning as I have written or ten times treats with burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is of this kind. Heat the iron in this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "close" because the head is made in the shape of a cross or with .1 inch of curvature and a small size; and place it on the painful area, hold your hand and move the iron slightly, but not too much so that half of its thickness burns; and withdraw your hand so that the arteries do not burn, which is away from it, and let blood flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After putting cotton in the wound and leaving it for three days; then put dampened cotton on top of it; and heal the shoulder with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this dislocation using the cautery called "cultellare", all around the tip, be careful not to touch the artery in this dislocation which should not be old.
de emigraine	of the dislocation
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating dislocation as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases and it does not improve, and you see that cauterizing before mentioned medicine and iron do not help, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and place it against the side of the wound with a line of half a finger's length, and press once with your hand without touching the artery and without going to the bone; beware of the jaw that stops speech when one eats, and do not let nerves have regard for the mute and spasms come to the patient, and beware of corruption of blood from the artery when it is cut or fear comes too much and especially to those who are not familiar with it, and are not students and tested; leave the operation in progress; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is explained in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter about the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	for the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear has pain due to coldness, and it has been treated with soluble medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pins", which is made as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After marking all around the sick ear, or around both of them where the pain is located, move away slightly from the root of the ear since you have signed the place; and place 10 points around each ear; after curing it until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth cautery
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	A cautery is only used to treat tumors that move due to fluid, as we have said in the classification of diseases; and do not apply a cautery to similar conditions arising from sores or nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture which mutes the flow of blood from eyes, and purges the head and throat, and this is ineffective, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little further from the temple, and the third at the junction of the lips; place the cautery on the part that opens healthy, and make the cautery towards the top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a fist; and leave the cautery until half of the hair is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the shape of the scalpel we have mentioned earlier, but it is slightly more subtle and the blades should be a little thicker; after treating the wound as I have previously stated, allow it to heal when it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	If apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the forehead, and one where the wound is called "vas" as we have previously stated, and the last cautery on the stomach mouth; treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	From the littera (or litterary)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	In this illness, give the patient large years and round pills made from the brain of a rooster; then place the plaster of mustard seed (sinapis) on the head of the patient, which is written or treated with plasters; and this is the way of cautery: if it is done as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is a wound in the head or neck, it is good; and if it is not, make four cauterizations of the vein on the head descending to the neck, with a space between each cauterization of two fingers wide; and cure it as others do; and if you see it needs more, make one in the middle; and if necessary, make two others over the two horns, and cure it until it is healed; and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" be as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head of the patient should be cleaned for years and as we have said before; after that, anoint the head of the sick person, then make a fire cautery on the head and one at each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the sick person is weak, and the disease is severe, do four cauteries on the spine of the back; leave it until the most painful part is burned, then cool your hand; after that, cure it until it is healed, and remove the cautery which is called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use a fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to modify the head with various treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and enduring to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, make them gargle and often chew food to modify the head; afterwards heat the skull with a pestle, and perform one cautery as we have said before, and one cautery on the fontanelle, and on each horn; and if the patient is outside and enduring, perform cauteries as I have said for him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cauteries be olive-oil according to the method that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, perform one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupt and large phlegms, then the cautery of such kind should be applied as we have said to those who suffer from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	If due to melancholy, the excesses decline towards melancholy and the body of the patient is wet, then give him something to drink by which the brain may be purified, according to what has been mentioned earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the king, let the patient's head be anointed with one linen cloth well made, also like a circle, place it on his head; and the patient should cross his arms, and he should be well held from all sides; after that, anoint him, using old butter of goats; and heat the cloth carefully, so that it can be tolerable for him to endure it; afterwards, empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with good governance, until he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you wish to perform cauterization in many places, do it all over the cautery. This method of cauterizing aggravates the brain greatly; then put cotton dampened with butter and linseed oil on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first with the signs I have said in the division, then you should begin and give the patient something purifying the head, and guard him from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding him to lie down on his back, make a fire cautery at the back of his head, and make two cauteries on the two temples where the swelling of the eye is located or if it's on one temple; and strike with the entire cautery all the veins and arteries that are underneath the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and take care to prevent bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it by your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and the incision of the cautery how to extend it; and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is made underneath the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the eyes' tears are old and accustomed and are above the veins, or they are near the arteries that appear on the forehead; and it is seen that it is cold, fleumatic superfluities, then you make the cautery as I said at the beginning of the awesending to the eyes: i.e., cautery under the forehead, and 2 cauteries above the temples, and 2 cauteries or haiterel beneath the 2 bones; and if necessary, cauterize skillfully above the eyebrows with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the body of the tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	If you treat it according to what we have said in the division and it does not help, then give a sick person 2 nightshades; after which, heat the head and make cautery or oil cautery on the head; and make 2 cauterizations called "clavilis" above the eyebrows, a little below the hairline; be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery known as "olivare". This is its shape:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to make two cauteries on the two serpents as long as they are; and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the eyes are converted into sweat, and they prick oil, and a cauterization is performed according to two methods, namely by fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in a healthy position; afterwards on paper draw a figure similar to the fennel seed, and it should be the beginning of the sign where the hairs are; then place cotton soaked in egg glair and musk-scented persillaire oil over the oil. Then heat the cauterizer according to the following form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure that you have signed several times, let the blisters be burned in that place; and the signs of the success of the work are that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted at the tip of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it for 3 days, then put soft cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed; afterwards, apply ointment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs come, and the paper is softened then repeat the cautery on that same place as you did earlier; and if the hairs are falling out, cauterize it until the paper is raised to its natural position, and they are even, and do not prick the hairs with oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical hot cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, from each one an ounce, grind them together well; and do it quickly so it does not cool, then spread it onto the form you made like the myrtle leaf, and put paper on top of it; if the patient has pain in one oil only, it should be operated on in one, and if in both as well; and put cotton soaked in egg white under the oil; and the patient's head should be kept healthy and you press your finger every once in a while showing above the medicine, and move it all the times when the patient feels burning sensation from the medicine, because it burns like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, administer the medicine to your arm.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting has passed, lift the arm and observe if the papyrus is raised in the same way as it was lifted by burning or incision; and if it is thus, it is good. If not, apply more medicine on the arm or the medicine has not worked yet, while your efforts are equal and your eyes focused; then place moistened cotton over the burned area until the blisters have cooled, afterwards treat the arm with ointment called "dyafenis" and others until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful in your work so that the medicine does not drip from the hairs.  And if the papyrus becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, reapply the medicine on the area affected by the papyrus properly, as you have done before; afterwards heal it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the mirror-leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eye of men is diverse in size and smallness, according to which you should adjust your techniques; do not deviate from the correct path for him who is engaged in this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When curing a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on a clean surface and hold it still between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then put cotton soaked in egg white or fresh linseed oil on the area to be cauterized; after heating the cautery, apply it to the affected area shaped like the tip of a feather, ensuring that the cautery is also applied; if you see, it should be pointed from one side to the other, and if you see, it should resemble a tent; however, even if the cauterized area looks different, it still serves for your purpose.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, drain the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, drain the pus forcefully; afterwards place the hot iron cauterizer on top, keep your hand on the cauterizer at the part of the neck near the oil, so that your hands do not make a mistake; and place the cauterizer in the fat of the oil and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start the cautery up to the bone, it will be good. If not, continue the cauterizing once more and another time as needed, and leave it for three days; afterwards put cotton soaked in butter on top, treat the wound with drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days have passed without improvement, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way of cauterizing the fistula that none of the ancients spoke about. Understand this as a fistula, and cut the opening; afterwards put in the slit one thin camel's gall from which this formula comes:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make the quantity of one pound of plaster; hold your hand firmly and do not let the patient move at all, until the plaster solidifies; it is necessary that you place the oil on the patient's cotton wool soaked in egg white or water: the plaster will seal the wound, and the healthy part heals marvelously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the wound is healed by the cautery we mentioned, it is good. If not, it is necessary to administer purgatives and bring the wound to the body heat according to what is appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur in lips, which are called "poil," and also in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When treating these cracks as we have mentioned in the previous lines, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small cautery knife according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And immediately place it into these cracks until it reaches the bottom; then cover the area with cerote (cerotum) until it heals.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the eye, or palate, or roots of the teeth, after becoming purulent and growing and turning into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not improve: then it is necessary that you have .i. cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards plug or close the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron becomes hot at its source, and beyond it; and do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, you must discover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the slight movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but it does not help, put the head of the patient in a warm bath; after heating the cautery, shape it like a cane and place it on the tooth; then insert the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards release your hand and repeat the cautery as desired; afterwards fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse frequently.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such manner, the teeth that are moving should be immobilized, and the gums made soft and relaxed, and the moisture corrupt dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold or there is cold or fever, and the medicines have no effect, then it will be necessary to use cautery according to two methods: cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow and the end in a copper or iron spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent (small cloth), and wet it in boiling butter, and put it on the painful tooth immediately and hold it until it is cooled; and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see the cotton and cotton in cold butter, and put it on the tooth again, and put hot iron on it until the heat comes to the surface of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	1. "The fire cautery is as follows: take a rod of iron or brass, and it should be thick so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, the shape will come next, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that day itself or the following."
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	"And perform the cautery on whichever head you wish, and according to your ability; and this is the form of the rod:"
des scrophules	"of scrofula" (referring to a condition that can cause swelling in the neck, possibly tuberculosis)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of a fluid and cold moisture, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery hair as described below, and have two openings for the smoke to issue from the other side; and place the heated cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the base of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, use cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it as such for three days; and apply soft cotton soaked in butter until the pain subsides; afterwards cure the place with ointments and poultices until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the humors prevail in the channels of the throat, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be purged by soluble medicines; afterwards make cautery at the root of the throat, but do not go up to the throat and only use a little bit of heat. Afterwards make another cautery at the joint between the neck and the spine, and it is called "clavile" according to our previous form; and cure the place as previously said until it is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and sickness of the worm are due to cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor heat, and the disease is old, you should perform two fire cauterizations on the forcible joints; and another cautery between the two breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavile" according to the form mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you wish, perform cautery by pricking all the cautery called "poins" of the form mentioned earlier in the disease of the ears; and let the poins be up to 30 or more, around it. After curing the joint as previously said, let the cauterization be at four intervals according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, because you make four at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After placing the patient on his back and on his side, press the cavity that is within the thigh with your left hand's fingertips; if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the fire cautery in the shape of two needles as shown here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and the dislocation will be corrected with these four fire cautery tools; it is made with the cautery that has two needles, because the shape of cauterization consists of several cauteries; and the nerves are shaped according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the cautery that has two needles:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is cauterized above this, namely the nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the cautery, break it with silk; then make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	If it is dislocated above (the shoulder), which happens rarely, then apply cautery on the thick part of the caution splint or many cauteries in pricking. For the joint is repositioned, the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that one should perform cauterizations on the pleura using roots of Aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest you can find, and it should be dry and as large and long as your thumb; moisten it in oil, heat it up, and cauterize one cautery between the chest and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the area below the beard; two cauterizations on the fifth costal cartilage and the sixth, declining slightly; one cautery on the bladder, and one more on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on each side of the bladder, but not the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, instead, be gentle as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	Some ancient men said that one should use a cautery resembling a razor and heat it up, placing it between the ribs until it reaches an abscess; but the pain subsides as we have mentioned in the liver abscess. However, in this work, there is fear or the patient dies now, or fistula appears that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice as we have said in the divisions of care, and it does not help at all, then apply three ways of cautery, which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	One of the ways is that you make four or six cauterizations in a row, according to the length of the mouse, following the shape of the cautery of the liver as we have said before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, let the patient be conscious on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; take the cavity where the patient's swelling comes towards the left side, and lift the cavities from there according to the cavity, following the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After setting the two inflamed nerves on fire until they are pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, thus having four; if you see, cauterize the entire cautery to three nerves.  After the cure when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth noting that the other cures mentioned before should be done first.
de ydropisie	Diuretics
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cauterizing does not help with edema (dropies), except in the way called "asclytes". If you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in the divisions, and your cure is of no benefit, then you must do four cauteries around the liver, one on the stomach, one on the spleen, two behind the back near the spine, and one in the area of pain; and ensure that the cauteries are well placed near the thick part of the kidney.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the fire cautery heal for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; healing would hasten and the two intentions will be combined with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the claw as we have shown before; and for the back it is olive-shaped, according to what was mentioned above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in one who is edematous, and filled with watery citrus fluid, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deep, lest the watery citrus fluid spreads too far, and let the cautery be in this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauteries in each leg at the tip of the index finger; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and another outside the leg; and leave the cauteries above for a while to heal, so that the water drains out; afterwards cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the swelling
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the swelling of the belly comes from cold and moisture, while the digestive and retentive qualities that are in the stomach and intestine are inhibited, and it cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having strong symptoms, then do this: make one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before (cautere of the stomach), or cauterize around the belly, in a circular manner; and four subtle cauteries around the navel, one subtle cautery at the clavicle, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see excessive moisture and the patient suffering, do a cautery on the elbow, one on each arm, and two small cauteries on the stomach, near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when aid is available.
de la cure des emorroydes	Treatment of hemorrhoids:
