Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are deep-rooted, whether one or more, and they are old and filled with large cold and corrupted humors, and as we have said in the previous sections, they cannot be cured; it is beneficial to perform cauterization: 4 on the spine of the back, which is completely exposed beneath the almecdate pouch and triangulated, and 1 caution below the navel. 2 doses;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think the stomach is chilled and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then a large caution should be applied to the stomach as described previously, and another to the liver, and another to the spleen entirely with a cautery claw; leave the caution open for a long time. After curing the wound, let it heal when it is clean.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut an artery, take the fire-cautery that appears like a razor and then burn it all over the artery you are cutting; leave your hand there so the tip of the cautery comes to the vein opening, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much blood, cauterize each time as we have said; afterwards, treat with healing herbs until they heal completely; and if you cauterize a large area with a large fire-cautery, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	of an unhealed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When a patient cannot endure such large incision or opening, as we shall explain in its place, comes the sickness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes, and it is filled with pus and corrupted moisture, one must test the entire extent of it subtly, and be aware that you know the entire extent of the opening to the fullest. After heating the cautery which seems like a razor, put it into the fistula according to the size of the opening that the pus has entered, and continue to heat the cautery until the body part and corruption are burned, once, or twice, or three times, depending on the amount of pus needing treatment; beware of burning the nerves that are there, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these places, and do not treat them outside the charned area, think that it is not persistent; after treating the area until it is healthy, if the area is seared and the material has been removed for a long time, know that the area is completely healthy; but if the material has not been removed, know that the area is cut, and the bone is corrupted at that point; and in this way, as one of those we will say about it.
de la maladie des reins	kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the flank comes with large swelling and does not take on female form, then it is necessary that you make a cautery over the kidneys from both sides using the cautery claw as we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be 4 cauteries in a line, and they will provide more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder becomes soft and weak from cold or moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a fire cautery in the area outside the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left, each cautery should be as long as a thumb; and make one cautery behind the back, if necessary; and make the cauteries incisions like the shape previously described.
de la marris	of the anus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term ends late; and when they come, then it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the womb, as we have said, or cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauterization be with a hot iron, as we have said.
de la hainche	The pustule
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures flow towards the abscess of the pustule and cause it to move from its place, the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the source can be found by sight. If you need to cauterize the patient over the abscess of the pustule at one cautery resembling a circle, with the sign pointing before the place around the abscess as it turns, so that the abscess is within the circle; and let the cauterization be similar to that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present for you, make 4 large olive-oil cauterizations instead, and let them be as deep as all the others; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain from the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hernia bag, it is due to coldness and moisture; the sick are healed with what we have said above in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary that you purge the sick person from the gross humors using fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the cautery, its method is in two ways: either with burning substances, or fire cautery. Fire cautery is done in various ways, one of which is as follows: you shall cauterize on top of the boil on the haunch, four triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make a deep and wide incision between each cautery that is the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautery is done in the middle on top of the boil on the haunch, for which there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, if you cauterize with the circular cautery that we have mentioned in the dislocation of the haunch, but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire haunch, and all the edges should be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is how one does it in sciatica when the pain is in the haunch and cannot reach the thigh nor the leg. If the pain comes to the thigh and the leg, two cauteries should be done where the patient says that the pain lies, and one cautery above the ankle 4 fingers, with a small space on the left side; let the cauteries be scalpel-shaped, and burn the thickness of the skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toe or near it, cauterize where he feels the pain 2-4 fingers or 4 in the cautery which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform a fire cautery using either a knife or circular device, and be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on too long so as not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I have seen many who have performed a cautery on the foot of the leg and left it too long, causing the entire leg to swell, as well as the toes, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted. After a belly solution in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform a cautery on one and the other in this manner. // The wise men say about the cautery of the shin, here is the method: make one iron rod with a head as thick as a nail of the thumb or slightly smaller, and be crosswise or between-crosswise at a distance equal to the width of a walnut; and the crosspieces should be four parts wide and shaped like nuts, and have a single handle of iron well made. This is its shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be scalded until it is all red and boils, and then put it on top of the sick man's haunch, and turn it over to the healthy side; and cauterize once with a fire cautery, and leave it for four days; then make a plaster of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; afterwards, cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to fear of its appearance and not many who use it; but this is a good cautery for those who can bear it, and where it should be applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or from striking or from excessive evacuation, or from similar causes of cold matter, none of these similar causes are worth cauterization, unless it is caused by the influx of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be bled of fetid pills or similar, and make it on the back where the pain is located, three inches marked with incisions, and in each line five or more cauterizations according to the power and quantity that the patient can bear; and the cauterization should be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do four cauterizations or four on the cautery called "clavile moien" in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrowed anus when they defecate, and fear; you can find it in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance that appears above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this [object] and wish to cure it, if necessary, use the fire cautery in this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Increase the size of the fire cautery on each part of the spine. And if you see, apply the cautery around the spine, pointing .2 or .3 inches, with the tips close to each other. After that, cure the area until it is healed as we have said, and be careful not to use a cautery in a glandular area containing nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is from swelling affecting every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and it is caused by coldness and medicine cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the patient prepare a cautery around the joint of the foot, and the cautery should be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If it is necessary to prick the face of the foot, prepare a cautery all over the foot, which is called "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens often, prepare a cautery on each knee. Four cauteries or four from each part should be olive-shaped; and if you need more, do more, but hold your hand only as long as the tips of the coal are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains extend to the knees and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and consider medicines. For if you give good care and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's aid.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the breaking of the siphac (or siphunculus)
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the hernia comes in anguish, and the bulge descends into the groin and this happens suddenly, if you want to treat it, you must not let him eat anything that day; you should use things that relax the abdomen so the stool passes from his stomach. Afterwards have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to cling to his loins as tightly as possible until the bulge has receded, then press it to your sides, and apply pressure on top of the hernia above the joint of the little finger, and at every sign that is similar to half a circle on the chest. Then heat the cautery in the shape that is shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and gives out sparks (or flames). Then press the bulges back to their place; and have the assistants hold his hand so they do not return. Tightly bind both his thighs to the patient, put a cushion and a belt on his thighs, and another one around his waist that holds his hands. Then place the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, holding it straight and until you reach the bone. If you do not touch the bone at first, try again until you reach it; be careful that the bulge does not come out while you are applying the cautery. Do not burn it, and make sure the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And the cauteries for children should be fine-tuned according to their size, and for adults according to theirs; after 3 days, cure the place of the cauterization with butter until the burn is healed; after that, cure it with other unguents until it is healthy; and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days, so that the wound may heal well; and it is necessary to allow his excrements to be delayed, so that the feces do not protrude when he gets up to go to the rooms.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, provide him with a well-made strap and keep it for another 40 days; let him rest well, so that he does not work too much or eat and drink too much, nor talk too loudly; and when he follows these instructions, he will be completely healthy. And I will say more about the treatment of amputation in its chapter afterwards.
de la routure dou ventre	of the cutting into the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When roundworms come into other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, then let one fire cautery be made according to its quantity, and it should be burned the third part of the belly; afterwards, cure as we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at four angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	Mark the place of the worm and make a line above it in width over the roundworm, and another below it, and press your hand all along the cautery handle. But the first cauterizations are lighter and easier to move.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, either due to falling or being injured, and that pain lasts for a long time and the medicine does not work, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member, its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location of twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that is good; if not, repeat another cauterization on top of it, as this is the custom, because the member nearest to the wound should change, so you must perform the cauteries until the patient heals.
de meselerie	When a wound occurs due to cutting or an injury, and pus comes out of it, and the limb surrounding the wound becomes inflamed, then it should be dressed with the medicine called "meselerie," and the dressing should cover the wound entirely, and the dressing should be applied daily until the wound heals.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The poultices are sometimes aided by cautery with great help, and the same applies to illness that comes from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you observe it starting, be careful and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither pus nor decay remains, then apply five cauteries on the head: one at the top of the head, another near the front towards the end of the hair; two on the temples, and one at the back of the skull; leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and let the scabs come out until the vapors of the large humors can escape; then cauterize the mice according to what is described.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the swelling is spread out everywhere; it clearly indicates that you must burn with these cauteries which we have said: one on the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and one small one, and two on each shoulder; two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of nerves that are above the ankles, do not burn them; sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the fist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Know that the more cauteries you do, the more help it gives, and it is beneficial to him; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary that the cauterizations be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the art of iron smithing. After curing the wound with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
de enfleure	inflammation or swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When a swelling appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils and plasters but remains unhealthy, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be slightly deep into the flesh. Then cure it with ointments until it becomes healthy. And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand, foot, back, at the nerve's opening that makes the limb numb, and in this way the swelling is removed; but no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	When a boil or abscess breaks open and is left to heal on its own without treatment, and it remains swollen, then apply leeches to the affected area according to its size; and let the leeches suck until the swelling goes down. And sometimes leeches are applied to the hand, foot, back, at the opening of the nerve that makes the limb numb, and in this way the boil or abscess is drained; but no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the nerves moving the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" appears and the medicine devices do not work, then cauterize it with a deep cautery according to the size of the affected area until the blister is removed and its color changes; then apply a poultice made from barley flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, along with goose blood and woodpecker blood, of each one part; mix everything together, tie it in a cloth, and place it at the affected site until it becomes healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of scrofula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When scrofula begins and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that looks like a circle surrounding the entire scrofula, although some wise men say that cautionery should also be done in the middle of the scrofula; but I do not think it is good because it may ulcerate and corrupt it, and I have seen this happen once; a more appropriate thing is to cauterize around it, with the cautery called "circule", as we have said in the discussion about cautioneries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow larger
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," which is slow to heal or because of the superfluous matter it makes or because of the patient's age when they are decrepit (meaning very old) and have little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely with the cautery, then heat the cautery in this manner:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels the course of the pus to be cleared. Afterwards, cure it perfectly when it is healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure for fire is with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", which is simply a consumption of a limb, for it weakens the limbs just like fire burns dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where cautionery with fire can be used, then cauterize the cauteries little and large, according to what is required at the location or where the illness is; after the cauterization of all parts until you have reached all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that everything corrupted should be removed. And then leave it for 3 days, and apply a soft ointment made from cauterized lees soaked in oil to the affected areas until the burns caused by fire are removed, and all the corruption. After the cure of the medicine-induced ulcer has healed. And if after 3 days you see that healthy tissue has not grown, it is good; and if this is not the case, then repeat the cauterization on the part that remains corrupted. And this consumption can sometimes be cured with a hot medicine instead of fire-induced cautionery; however, fire-induced cautionery is of greater aid. I have already said the cure for the hot medicine in the division: take as needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	drops that come to the feet.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often happens that in the feet, a disease called "clos" arises according to our understanding, and it is a large thing that bites the foot. And the cauteries for this disease are according to .ij. ways. This means cautery by fire, and cautery by hot water. Cautery by fire is that you heat .i. cautery comb as thin as a feather of a small bird, made of good iron so that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and that it has fine edges; after that, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it like this for .iij. days until it begins to emit pus; then make a plaster of bad herbs crushed with oil, and leave the plaster on it all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from their roots. Then cure the place with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If it is transformed by moisture on the outside of the body, and often happens in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery by hot water; and it is in this manner: take a cane of iron or wood, or a feather from a small bird, and put it on the nail and press it, i.e., to remove warts; and put the cane on it so that it presses all around, then put a little hot oil on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in rotating so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water penetrates deeply to the root; and allow the patient a little the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will uproot all its roots. Do this again until you have heated all those in the body, then cure them with ointments that soothe.
li cure dou trembler	the cures for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or quartan fever, or other illnesses, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one cauterization at the heel, and one on the stomach using the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of putrid boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body shows external signs of bathing or putrid boils that come from corrupted matter. In such cases, it is necessary at first to make a cautery on each chief of the boil: a subtle cautery made with a myrtle stick, so the point is held in fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or the cautery lenticularis. Sometimes they are cauterized from the start according to this method, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter that comes from them is destroyed, and they become healthy; however, it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great flowings of blood from the cut artery at the wound or in the incision of the abscess or the cauterization of the member and similar things; it is a very bad thing to let it out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And although this happens in some cases, hasten to put your finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tight until the blood is stopped from flowing out; then take the olive oil cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then dip .i., whether large or small depending on the size and location of the wound where the artery is cut, in the oil and place the cautery on that vein while holding your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the wound suddenly jumps when you hold your finger on the vein and the cautery is extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing one after the other until the wound is healed; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is exposed, and that no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when a vein bursts from an artery, it cannot be well stopped at all, except by one of the four methods we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which can stop blood; and bind and hold it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever provides tight binding with strips of cloth or places hot things on it, or similar things, will not achieve anything beneficial if the bleeding does not stop.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this does not help and there is no remedy or medicine available, he must place his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it wide until the bleeding stops above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but let it be dampened with cold water often so that it becomes very cold, until the bleeding stops and thickens and stops; and make inquiries in advance about the necessary cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we explain the kinds of cauteries, their causes, instruments, forms, and types; I placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way because those things are easier to understand that way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to undertake folly. For many people come in for treatment. Some of them are so afflicted by their disease that they die easily due to the foolishness they find in their sickness, and from the greatness of its malice; and it is from these that fear should arise.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give you advice, and say: "Wait, I am cured." And the illness is deceitful. It is not right that you consent to those who come to you in this way, but put more concern for your honor than for your desire, and do not act rashly but wisely from those things of which you are certain, and from which you can take and lose; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is converted; and this will help you acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of his hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have divided this chapter into sections, in speaking of each section, just as I have written about the cauteries from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand what you need from that which is before you.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes upon children at birth, and when the head of the child is forcefully constrained; and sometimes it happens for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this illness in adults, and all those I have seen hastened to death; therefore, it seems worthwhile for me to describe the treatment in some cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant whose head was filled with water, and it swelled daily to the point that it could not support it; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed he would die, and this moisture is collected below the bone at the siphac, between the skull and the bone. Therefore, when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you must make a large incision over the head; let the size be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out. Here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is larger and the abscess is greater, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the incisions at each end of the abscess opening wide when pressed from within and it does not respond: then you must make four cuts in the middle of the abscess according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all the swelling outside. After that, tighten the cuts with bandages and powders, and put vinegar and oil in them, and leave it until the fifth day; then loosen it, and cure the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head swell gradually, and give the patient dried meat from the swelling as much as necessary until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the size of the abscess and gather the pus; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then take care that you do not cover the artery and make sure there flows blood, so that the patient dies a proper death by bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	diarrhea
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or worse, and the disease is old, and the medicine's cure does not help at all, then the last cure is the cautery, with which two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you see them, you must make the patient lean back; afterwards rub the place of two sharp fabrics on his neck until the arteries appear, then tighten the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the vein is biting, and the leves of one and the other are after the ears, and they are tied again; then mark the levels with a sign, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts. The cut should reach as far as the bone, and this should be wide through the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, making a cut similar to two fingers wide across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps continually outwards without ceasing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at will, then you must measure the space of three fingers, then press and pierce up to the bone; and that amount of blood to be forced out is 7 cubic centimeters, and possibly a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains on the bone point by point, if the hot iron does not enter, then hold and bind the wound and cure it with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and the acute catarrh arrives, due to moisture in the eyes, heat in the temples, old foolishness and similar things; it is treated with methods of medicine but none of it helps; if arteries from the temples are cut and cauterized as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should lie down with his/her hair on the temples and pay attention to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not easily found except in some cold people; and if it is found, the patient should tighten his/her neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula as shown in the following form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then lightly peel the skin to expose the artery, and pull it up towards the tweezers, and carefully separate the threads that are below each part; if the artery is thin, turn it at the end of the tweezers, then cut from that side according to the number of stones. For if it is not cut, it will not be moved completely in all places.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the 5th vein, up to the 3rd one; and if the artery is large, then you must tie it with a strong double thread of silk, so that pus does not come before the wound closes and there is flowing of blood; then remove the surplus between the 2 ligatures in the same hour itself, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the wound with the cautery cutlass up to the bone, but this is the hard work, if the patient does not have a fever and he has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are help for treating moisture: therefore it is of great help to those with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the area with old cotton and place a well-made tourniquet on it; and when you loosen them, they should be cured with dry medicines that produce char, and bandages, until it is healed; and if without cutting the artery as you perform, hasten to cover it with cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze it with your hand so that the area becomes discolored; and if this is not available, place your finger on the area for a long time until it freezes, and rub the area with cold water until it stops, and then squeeze it as necessary; and the hard and more difficult part in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery of 2 parts, but they should be well thickened to keep their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the straw is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two blades, one of a thick gap, and then when you have signed [the wound] for two leagues, and you place the heated iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be spaced apart because it is not glued with this cautery throughout; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the eyes' tears are flowing from the veins that are above the testicle of fire, and medicine does not help in treating them; you see the patient writhing in pain, and his forehead sweating as if with fever; and if they are soft and moist, so that the hairs on the scrotum have fallen out, and the scrotum is burned, scalded by the heat of tears, it requires this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And it will be called by the ancients "contused cure," and you shall make incisions at the back of the patient who has this disease in the hairs on his forehead, then make 4 equal fissures along the length of the forehead; one of these fissures as two fingers all the way down from the forehead to the nose, and the other two as two fingers across the scrotum above the testicles, being careful not to cut the arteries that are on the sides of the scrotum; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and each wound should be the size of four fingers joined together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a sponge piece and much of linen cloth for wiping the blood, then insert the sharp spatula of two fingers in this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape the entire core that is between the two cuts all the way up to the bone, then continue from the mid-incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatulumile (spatula).
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the tool called "cultellaire" into the first incision. It is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other side, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place the sharp side towards the flesh and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the mid-incision. And cut all the vessels that descend from the cartilage towards the hairs until the incision is complete up to where it opens the core, and then continue in the mid-incision until the other end; and then press the blood equally and identify the level for the blood drawn; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put moist cloths soaked in vinegar and oil on top, and make sure that there are no abscesses present; three days later, untie the suture, and apply a large amount of strong ointment made with basilicon oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh comes commonly, and you see the thin and small hairs falling out, and the vision becomes cloudy, and burned paper-like spots; and the hair follicles itch, and when the head hurts with intense pain, and the patient coughs; then know through these symptoms that those materials and that catarrh do not come from anything but many veins, and the remedy for the cure that is there, if it exists, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you instruct the patient to bend his head back, then make a large incision along the forehead, and another deep one. [Take] about half an inch of cloth and begin from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then insert cotton between the two lips of the incision and hemp thread; then place moist linen cloths on top, and be careful not to cause an abscess to heat up; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of turmeric, and make a poultice with them; administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for the unstopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains or animals, or stones or similar objects like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils; or something flowing like water and sand and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear, stone or any other thing that does not fit in the ear, nor enters the ear, place the ear on the sun. If you see a stone, distill a little drop of violet oil or camphor oil, then apply extraction; and make it vomit with mustard, and stop up the nostrils when vomiting comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear above. Often farting occurs through this cure; and if it does not fart, extract it with subtle tweezers as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not fart through the tweezers, extract it with thin wire of small length; and if it does not through this method, make a cane of wax and push its tip into the ear forcefully or through the ear canal, and stop up that which is around the cane with molten wax so that the wind cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out in the form of farting, for often it farts as we have said; and if it does not fart in this way, take glue of any kind and put it on anything that you find, and place any instrument sharp at the end over it; then put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not fart through any of the things we have said, hasten to open the ear before the abscess comes and spasms; and the method of opening is that you first make the patient sneeze the cephalic head, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small opening in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the opening be as a moon, so that you come to the stone, then extract it with your strength, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is an abscess that swells, administer drainage; and if it cannot be drained, administer a thin, fine spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make an incision if you think the abscess is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made several incisions; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is clean.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear when water falls, the patient should use hot fumigation with first condensers and fill the ear with cotton. Let it rest on that ear itself or the water will flow out. If it does not, take many pebbles according to the length of your finger and boil them slightly; then place one or two of them in the patient's ear and press another pebble against the one inside the ear; continue to do this with pebble after pebble until the water comes out completely, and it will flow out entirely; if you see, take a stick, and push one of the ears into the ear, and heat the other end of the stick with fire until the stick is burned; then repeat this process with other sticks until all the water comes out, as we have said in the pebble treatment.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals, such as fleas and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, bring about extraction with tweezers; and this is the lightest thing that can be removed from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and the cure does not improve, if you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers; but if there are none, take this substance's cord:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	Make it narrow inside and wide outside.
