Insert the most subtle part of the cord into the ear according to the severity of the patient's discomfort, then firmly draw out all the cord; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out. If they do not comply with coming out, stuff cotton around the cord as I have said in the previous section; and if they still do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the treatment of worms, and you will find them where I treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear using this apparatus as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And silver or tin is to be placed under a small hole, and above a receiver for distillation; and for pressing within the distillation there should be an instrument of tin well made for this purpose. If you wish, take a scraper and wind it around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish in the canal, which should be in the ear. Then push the scraper into the cotton, and press gently until the oil is distilled or has risen to the ear. The patient will feel the heat within. The distillation should be heated with fire in the same way as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective if it were cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (or ear drops)
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without ear problems; and this same thing happens in men due to ear wounds or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes comes suddenly into the ear, if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small amount of discharge from the ear, which can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes in full (meaning the disease), if one cannot see it, is grave in many conditions and when one can see it, you must place the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation (pustule) apparent, then open it entirely with this spatula of which the form is as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and pointed in front and behind, so that it does not prick the ear; if the opilation is of pus or cartilage from the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers and gently press it until all the pus is expelled.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the pustule is inside the ear, take a subtle razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear. If you feel the pustulation that causes pain to the patient's hearing, make a small incision gently, but be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a plug according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make this every day until the wound heals, take a linen cloth and soak it in rose oil and powdered vitriol; if you see swelling on the ear, then you must pull out the linen cloth and apply another linen cloth soaked in oil of roses and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood which are either to treat with distillation.
de la char des papieres	of paper pulp
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy that comes in papers for the eyes when they are moist and dry; you should stretch them with tweezers and forceps, then strike their roots with a spatula; afterwards place vitriol powder on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not work without peeling, then cauterize with the subtle cautery of the lentil, and cauterize afterwards after the incision has healed; and many times they heal, yet nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	"Often come out of the eyes on paper things that seem hail-like in shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called 'hail', and it is a thick gathering of moisture in the upper and lower layers of the paper; the treatment is as follows: take care to ensure that the hail does not melt from one side or the other, and this is an easy thing to know; make a hole wide enough, then gently remove the skin from each side, then take the tweezers and grasp it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, do not worry the patient; if the tear is large, assemble it with stitches, and care for it until it heals; if it is small, do not apply force, because the ointment will restore it soon and prevent harm."
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"If the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and grasp the hail with tweezers and press from both sides; if the paper is pushed away by the incision, do not worry; when the hail is covered, apply salty oil, and care for the affected area until the patient is healed."
de la graisse des eulz	"of the fat of the eyes"
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is impregnated on fabrics made of paper, and it happens more often in children than in adults, and it causes them much discomfort, and they get catarrh at mornings, and cannot bear the light of the sun because tears quickly flow from their eyes; therefore, they lie down on their faces immediately, sleep, and have wet papers under their eyelids that cover the exinach which opens in oil. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The method of treatment is that the patient should place his head on your clean surface; then take one small linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then put it over him; press with your hands from both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture using a pointed spatula, but not too large, no larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin to where you see the exinach; and in several positions, the exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take hold of the entire piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to both sides until it is spread; and make sure not to tear in the incision, that you do not go all the way with the spatula up to the oil, that you do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, lift a little the incision gently until it opens; then pull out as we have said, then moisten gauze in water and oil, and place it on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And to those who break the oil and put it on to corrode the moisture that remains. Then heal it until it is healthy. And if an abscess heats up at the place, heal it with hot poultices until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs from the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper lice are born with hair other than nature's, and they grow, they harm the eyes, and cause illnesses such as customary tears and softening of the paper lice and albugo, which leads to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways of treatment: either by cautery along with fire, or by cold medicine according to what is stated in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by squeezing, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper lice from the oil to your left hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, push an awl through one filament of it; and cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs growing from these hairs, and pull one filament along the entire length of the paper, and shave it with a razor; then make an incision in the part underneath the paper, under the hairs, covering the whole spatumile, from the large tear to the small; then draw out one filament, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen beneath the paper, then mark upon the paper a figure similar to the mirte leaf, and it is essential that the figure be according to the quantity by which you want to lift the paper as described to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if you need to remove a large quantity of paper as the paper is softened; then make an incision along all the spatumile on the two lines that you have marked, starting from the large tear down to the small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then insert the onion into either angle of the keyhole, then peel it entirely; then stitch the two lips together with a needle and thread of fine linen at one filament, and squeeze out the blood, and attach any excess filaments to some gluey things, if you want to do this; but if not, leave the stitches and the filaments for 2 or 3 days; then treat the wound without stitching using drying and binding agents, as the paper rises again at the edge of the wound and its attachment, but the stitches are rotten (as the ancients say), and this is labor without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure like the fennel of myrtle, as we have said, three times drawing according to the form below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then join those who are above the small spaces equally according to the form below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with one thread, and push it through the figure; then take another thread from the large hole, and the second thread from the small, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over which you have signed, as we have said, then stitch the two edges of the wound together with suturing, and heal it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with a balm and similar soothing agents.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the head is converted: you must use what we have said about incision; however, stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of dogs is as follows: you convert the skin and turn it inside out as I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two thin threads as long as the skin and the width of the incision; and tie together the two ends with threads; then assemble one on top of the other subtly over what is above the skin of oil, and bind the two stitches from the two parts tightly; leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is tightened will rot and necrotize and fall off, leaving a hole through which it can heal.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time or you must force it, then cure it until it is healed; when the wound is closed, and the skin rises, and the hairs cannot be felt; and this is the form of the two stitches that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	1. The work (li ovraiges) is such that you take a fine needle, and put on it one thread of silk and fine; then assemble the heads (les chiés) and join them subtly, and let the lengths of threads be a palm long; then prepare another fine silk thread briefly, and join its ends; then place the patient's head in your hand; let the work be done in sunlight so that it is visible, for this work is subtle and minute; then push the needle to the base of the hair adjacent to the natural hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then remove the hair up to the base, and put the removed hair back into the hole in the paper, if there is any; then remove your hand until the hairs come out entirely from the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the case (la chasse) is treated and the hairs do not come out, you will draw the case to below, along with the thread that you have prepared, until the case comes out through the opening made and you see it through oil vision; then you will draw the case and the thread, close the oil, and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and the flesh grows over; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair, and let them grow together, until they are elongated and then shave them.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or porridge comes in the oil, it has two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly through a wound, or through cutting, or cautery, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of treatment for this is that you cut that joint, separate its lips, and put in linen threads, and keep it until it heals; it should not be used in the treatment of it with things that dry and restrict. For if you do so, the disease returns worse than the first time; but works of softening things, such as fenugreek; and the broth of water or milk and flax seeds are cooked, and immediately afterward, castor oil melted into any oil is added to it, and a linen wrap is made from this, and this is used for treatment.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your cure is that you do not allow it to heal in its original form; and this treatment that we have described is not without caution against this disease returning in its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fat that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath [described as] "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accidental part comes from wounds, fissures, cauterization, and similar things; and the procedure in it [the disease] is that you take a needle, with which there should be a double thread, and thrust it into the fat, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two folds of the fat; then the fat should be raised above the entire needle, and [you] apply a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks where the costal cartilage lies within the paper; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the four angles of the incision that you have made, and let them form an angle such that when they are assembled, the shape should be like the shape of a letter which has the name "y greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to the amount it protrudes from the paper; then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then apply the medicine for softening as we have said before, and heat, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a crack or incision or cauterization, then you must make a smooth cut beneath the hairs of the paper, as described before; then you should split apart between the two edges of a tent, as I have said; and the work must be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare engines with all their power as they know how to bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is required for the work and various instruments.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bond occurs in the hand of men in such a way that the paper is stuck together with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to insert the point of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it between pliers until you cut the adhesion which is near the spatumile, not too sharp or too deep so as not to cause pain to the patient from the sharp spatumile; and make your incision, by which you scrape the assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal the entire assembly, and salt the oil at times, lift fresh sweet oil, and colyrium; then place a linen tent between the paper and oil, and put above the oil wool moistened abundantly with egg yolk; and after the third day use the colyrium and the healing substances until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail has two types: one is nervous and resembles a hard horn-like growth, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moist matter that when touched with iron and cooked with pliers, it cannot be removed; and both start from the large root, and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places their head on your hand, then you pull out the hairs; take paper in your hand, then bend the nail over with small tweezers, and hold it up; then take a needle, put a horse hair or ox or cattle hair and a strong thread on it; bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce the nail, poke through the entire needle, tie the nail with a thread and hold it up, then scrape off all the skin surrounding the nail root including silk and wool to the head; then chop the remaining in the root of the nail at the spatula-like tip and the small forces, leaving the natural flesh or nail, so that the incision does not bring forth tears as is usual; sometimes the nail is only set on the onyx, and at the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft spatulum around it as described in this shape.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatulum does not touch the flesh layer and break it, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision pour some broken oil and ointment made from litargire on it, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter it, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take a spatula-like tip slightly sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently scrape the nail above, and if you see that it does not lessen at all and the reason is pursued, distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litharge and red collyrium powder and boiled, and stop up the oil until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing goes against you in the oil as in an abscess, then let it heal on its own, and first treat the abscess with warm remedies until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the oil greatly, suspend it at the onion, and crush a part of it but not too much, so that tears do not come; then distill into the red collyrium oil made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men, flesh sometimes grows red and covers the eyelid and presses against the eyeball and turns it outward, resembling a baluster rose; and the procedure is such that the patient places their head in your hand, then you open the eyes, and cut all the growing flesh with cautery-like instruments appropriate for this purpose, and hold it with force; then cut the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting to the root until the end, taking care not to wound the oil gland at the operation; and let the incision be a spatula-shaped one as we have said in the incision of the nail, and the small tools used for removing the nail, as shown by the form described in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of ointment crushed or distilled red collyrium resembling corrosive medicines, and place cotton soaked with egg white on top to ensure that the wound heals without infection; if anything remains, and the wound becomes infected, and you doubt whether it will heal properly, leave the oil and treat the infection with soothing remedies for healing wounds; then return to your work when the wound is healed, and do the same for all such cases of eyelid growth in the oil in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in every case, it is necessary that you be cautious of the treatment for each weak part of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work with iron; and do not strike your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The red veins that are covered over the eye take away its work and weaken the eye all day long. Therefore, it is necessary at first to examine whether the eye, in which the vein is, is healthy and has no other disease but the vein; then cauterize it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then press those veins all along according to your wisdom, and let them be subtle double as shown here:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two times in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then let these veins be handled delicately, and suck out the blood an hour after another, until you see the veins move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that no heat remains but the veins themselves; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red collyrium to cure those who are congealed.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to suck out all of it in that hour, apply a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and assured of healing, then continue according to this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula from oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The term for "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have said earlier, and it is not healed, there is a trap in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the tools mentioned earlier to reform it; and it is called "sharp head", and it should be made in the form of a pointed chief, and sharpened like a chisel as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the rotten bone part on top, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand slightly until you feel that the corruption is restored; do this once, then restore the bone with medicinal pressure.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is healed and char grows around it, and the body of the wound remains closed for 40 days without becoming abscessed or infected, knowing that it is healthy; if this is not the case, there is no other remedy but to return the fistula to its original place according to this form: you must expose the bone a second time with iron and medicine heat, and when it is exposed, take one rod according to this form, and let the iron be pointed at three angles, and let the shaft be attenuated to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the rod on the bone near the edge of the wound, and move your hand away from the oil by a little bit, then turn the rod completely so it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the bone with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the char grows and hardens the bones, the matter goes to the nose; it will be easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the flow of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If all the eyes (meaning openings in a body part, such as wounds or abscesses) are fully opened and there is no need to dislodge anything or lessen it, then you must tie up the patient; next, heal him, apply hot poultices or plasters with iron to help, then apply oil (made of ingredients like acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla); then hold the oil, and apply the poultice on bandages and cloths. The manner of the cloths should be that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and place one on top of another according to the size required by the eyes; then bind them with a tough bandage and repeat the hot poultices and plasters and the oil and the cloths and the bandages until the eyes are healed. If the bandage weakens, you must tighten it more; if the bandage wears off after a day or night, you must remove it and see if the eyes heal over again. If they do, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice, the cloths, the bandages and the oil until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the breaking of woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the ruptured eyeball, it opens up and fumes like grains of resin, and is frightening to see; then if you cover it, the treatment is such that you push an awl into the root of the affected part all the way to the top, then push another awl where there is a double thread from the limbus; pierce it, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then hold the eye tightly with the double thread and wrap a portion of the eyeball around it, tightening it well, then pull out the awl and put oil-soaked woolen yarn on it abundantly; and leave it until the threads adhere with the eyeball, then treat the oil with comforting substances until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the eyeball itself in a circular bandage of fabric until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes appear swollen, pierce them with a thin spatula that comes from oil, remove the moisture and clean the eyes, then enter immediately; then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from the oilbowl, appearing like an abscess draining but not being an abscess; and the appearance of its work is that you make the patient sit on a chair fitted and straight, then take hold of his head between your two hands, and move it until you see the oilbowl come up towards your eyes; then let it be lanced, and unstop the light, and let the patient observe things as he usually does; and if it does not drain, know that it is an abscess, and if the draining of the oilbowl is not prepared as we have said. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtile spatumile and put it on the corneal cloth .i. a span along the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal cloth and the crown, until the oilbowl comes out; and when it is issued, let it distill into the hot oily honey mixture or water boiled with honey, or fenugreek water boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	oil abscesses
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of abscesses in the division and what is needed to perforate it; do according to its health. You must make the patient sit with his arms crossed, away from light due to the sun, and press the oil gently and tightly; then put the paper of the oil on your left hand if the hair is on the left side, or on your right hand if the hair is on the right side; then take in your right hand (if the hair is on the left side) the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand (if the hair is on the right side); then place the point of the instrument under the cornea at a distance of one finger width from the inner corner of the eye, towards the lesser eyelid; then push the almagda instrument vigorously and hold your hand firmly until it penetrates through the cornea, and feel that the almagda has reached the empty space; and the measure of the passage of the almagda should be at the full length of the measurement from the prunele to the end of the nose; this is the cornea of the oil; you will see the bone in the paper due to the brightness of the corneal cloth, and then put the instrument up to where the abscess is, and press it forcefully down a passage after that. If the abscess drains now, the patient can see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a brief rest, and if the second vein rises again, place the force with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently twist your hand around; then put a little of the gemstone oil inside. Then apply oil soaked or damp cloth, in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind with the oil. We, and those from our time, place on top commin crushed with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the gemstone oil cannot enter due to its hardness, since there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must take the tool called "alberit," which is shaped as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, only pierce the conjunctive and do not go too deep, but make it subtle first, then insert the gemstone; and when the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep by having him lie on his back in a dark room; and be aware of all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to either side, and tie him according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in the same dark room, test his sight, show him some things, and then re-tie him for a week; do not do this during the treatment or immediately after the incision, but rather loosen it because the blood rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess breaks open, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it towards that which soothes an abscess; and when it is appeased, you should lance the eye (incision) and put a small linen cloth over it for one day, and stay in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and convert to his case; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country people make almagda perciet, so that the juice comes out, but I never saw any such thing on our land, nor have I heard of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And here are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly from arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these [should be] of the same subtlety, and the backbone in four angles bent.
de la char sor le neis	of the neck on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Never are or nasal charms born diverse, of which some seem like scorpions at the mouth of feet; and if there are such [charms] or a charm inflamed with black color, and if it is a soft charm of good color. In this case, for these soft chars that are not inflamed, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the onion juice onto those chars, and drag them out; then take what you can hold with the sharp, subtle spatula, until you know that the charm is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any substance that cannot be covered, open it with all sorts of subtle and light instruments so that nothing remains; and if without your notice, or the abscess swells, aid it as necessary; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the pus dries up and all the charred matter is removed, then pour in oil, vinegar or cool water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the poison enters into the palace (skull), know that it is sick; and if the poison does not perforate as necessary, know that char has grown in the bone above, so instruments do not come to cut it: then you must insert a large thread of flax, well greased with your hands, and have intervals of one thumb's width between each stitch; and put the patient's head into the thread in its nostrils as far as it can go, and draw it out while smelling for the poison to come out through the nose; and children at school often do this, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold one head with one hand, and the other head with the other hand, and know one after the other by us who are at the thread. Do this until you know that the stitches have corrupted the char; then pull out the thread, squeeze out the blood, and immerse the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that remains of char; and then put oil or a plaster of some kind over it for as long as it is sick, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, as they say when distilling oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or lead, resembling a lamp with an open top, like a funnel, and guide it accordingly; and if you see, make the funnel closed, and let the instrument be filled for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh upon the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often on the head of the neck arises a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to look at; and because of this, you must cut it open at the beginning, and completely remove it, then put in place the fire cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay too long when it becomes large, take care if it is hard, dark colored, insensitive: do not touch it with iron as it is an aggravated abscess, for when it is cut open once, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch and not dark colored, you can cover it all, fear the patient and treat the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilage joints, it is of little use except in some men. Therefore, if this happens to anyone, you should check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then you place the two lips together in a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already dislocated from one side and the other, you must sew up all the parts of their edge until they heal, then put the two lips together in a suture and hold them, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood, and incense crushed; and place powder on top of these powders a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster adhering, and leave it until it dries up, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To the human hands, it often happens inside the lips there is an abscess hard like grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you should turn the lips and cut above each tooth, take with forceps and strike in every part; afterwards use leeches after incision of vitriol powder, until the blood stops flowing; then apply the ointment of asafoetida and cure the wound with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	Of the skin around the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, there arises on the gums a type of skin that the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and strike its root, letting the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders to the area; if the skin returns after the incision and this happens often, cut it again and cauterize; it will not return after being cauterized; these are the shapes of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	The sores (or ulcers)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are collected at the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs which are ugly; and sometimes they are black and yellow and swollen as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and remove the sores or scabs that appear, as long as there is nothing remaining; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and the yellow and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have completely removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to be smoothed, according to the work that shows, because the razor used to remove the teeth from between them has other shapes than the one used to remove them; and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating the tooth for pain, you should delay drawing it out as much as possible, because it must not be done at all; since this is a very high substance and there should be no excuse for razing (or removing) it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to draw a tooth, you must be certain about which one to pull. Many times pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is a good tooth, but the pain does not cease even after the good tooth has been removed, for we have seen this happen with noblemen; and when you are fully certain about which tooth to pull, you must incise around the tooth all around. Use a strong spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then push it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the base of the tooth, little by little until it is well loosened, then tighten the pliers firmly; and keep the patient's chin in your hand so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After breaking the tooth, if it does not come out by itself, take any of these instruments and gently push it in from all sides, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and carefully tighten the pliers, so that it does not break while being pulled out; and you should work very carefully around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it (the tooth) and leave a part behind, which would cause the patient greater pain from the root than in the first instance. Be aware that you do not act like ignorant nobles, who by their haste and recklessness sometimes break the cart, and fail to perform what we have mentioned; but sometimes they bring about great disease due to the roots that remain or because of the cart they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or oil and lard; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, which mute the teeth at first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so they do not bend when used, and be of good iron, and toothed for holding them firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, then you must put cotton soaked in butter on it for 1 or 2 days until the butter is absorbed, then insert the tongs called "algefri", which resemble a beak of a pincer; and inside them should be made like a chisel, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these instruments, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the tool called "althali," meaning pliers, here is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be thick and large so as not to break it, and if the root pops out with these tools, that is good; but if it does not, then help with all the instruments, here are their forms following:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two prongs, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are placed before the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool must not break, and know that many tools of teeth are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their own instrument according to what their work and illness require, because there are various diseases where the ancients did not teach any instruments due to diversity among them; and if it breaks a chariot or another bone, which is possible, then he seeks the tools that are required, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy to hold the bone tightly, so that it does not slip away, but can be held and removed; and then restore the bone with appropriate medicine; and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then remove everything with this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and the form is ugly, even in young women, you should know if the tooth has not erupted after the milk tooth, and it is not properly aligned, and cannot be filed or trimmed; then extract it. And if it is accompanied with the tooth, take this instrument that is described as being similar to a small beak, made of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And press hard and hard for many days due to the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others; if it appears that it can be filed, file it with a small file as shown below:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently but firmly for many days until it loosens slightly; then smooth it at the end with any smoother, and if the tooth is excessively sharp and bites the tongue, you must file off the sharpness so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
