Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth fall out due to either being knocked out or falling, and the patient is unable to chew anything without them falling out again, and you treat them with medicines that restrict [the teeth], it is not effective; instead, they should be held in place with a gold thread, for silver threads become green and decay, but gold does not change; and let the thread be medium sized neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between two healthy teeth, then place the roots between the misaligned teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering it up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and carefully, so that it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then take the roots with the thread using pliers, assemble them, and place them back between the healthy tooth, making sure it does not bite the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if they slip out or the threads break, hold another thread in place; if it remains and serves for a time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy and two misaligned teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth fall out and are put back in place repeatedly as we have said; let no one who is not wise and patient interfere; and sometimes the shape of a tooth made from bone from a cow or other animal is placed where the missing tooth was, and it is held in place as described earlier, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	There is sometimes this ligament that comes under the tongue naturally or by accident due to a wound; and the treatments are such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head steady, lift the tongue; then cover the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and this is due to sudden wound, press the uncine and cover the ligament widely; and make sure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done so, lift the cool rose water or cold water, then put a linen tent under the tongue; and bandage him each night, so that the wound does not heal. And if there comes discharge of blood, apply vitriol powder; and if it persists, cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other medicine until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of short color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is declining towards blenchor (gangrene), and there is moisture, press the uncine, and cut it with a thin spatula from both sides; and if the wound persists at your treatment, apply vitriol powder until it is drained; then raise cool water or oil, and treat with other medicine until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes boils called "godath" appear inside the throat, which are properly called the two mandibles. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess with small sensation and reddish color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of bleeding; but let it remain until it is soft, and then you will cut it open or it would burst by itself; and if it is white-colored and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check if the abscess is cold and calm. Then make the patient sit in the sun, with his chest in your hand, and open his mouth and take hold of the mandibles between your hands, and press the tongue down on top of the instrument, which has this shape; it can be made of silver or fine bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue down on top of the instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the awl and insert it into the mandible, pulling it up more than you can; and pull anything from the cloths with it, then cover it with the instrument, which has this shape, resembling a fork; even though the neck is curved and one end is close to the other, and they are very sharp, they are made of iron or bone.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron tongs like this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron tongs in such a way: one part is named, and when you have grabbed one of the nuts (or bulbs), grasp the other in the same manner, then heat the wound with hot, sharp, and smooth objects, and if bleeding occurs, continue heating it until the bleeding stops; or scabs from pomegranate peels are cooked, or bay leaves, and similar things to stop the bleeding; then cure it until it heals; and sometimes more abscesses than two nuts grow in the throat, grasp them then equally as well.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside the throat, to be precise, a small abscess; and I had closed her throat entirely, so the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died in one or two days. The abscess was so high up that it had already formed two pockets through both openings of the throat. So I immediately made an incision, and inserted a hook through one pocket, then pulled out a large piece of pus; then I sealed the other opening of the throat, opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the hook into those abscesses, removed a portion, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus, the passage in her throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting the abscess for a long time; the abscess continued to grow back, filling the space I had vacated until it became very large; then I trapped it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus the abscess ceased growing; and I left those parts and let God heal them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye swells and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is subtle, then you must cut; and the one that is round swollen and not long; and it is bloodshot or of dark color or black, then you must make an incision in it. For there is great danger for the patient. It is therefore necessary, when you see, according to the manner I have said, of its swelling and length, to make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the hook into the eye, pull it out, and cut at .i. of .ij. places that I have said in the incision of the 2 arrows. And you must not cut more than the superfluous tissue that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, it hurts the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the 2 arrows, and treat it until it heals. And if the patient fears to be cut, then use an instrument for cauterization to lessen fear. And the manner of cauterization is hot. And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned or chapter on cauterization, and hold against a hot live coal, but not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, as shown in the following figure:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has hair in the eye, or oil is applied to it, as with the scoop of a spoon, and the instrument is placed on top of all the medicine over the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine without reaching the throat and nose; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it swelling and the bite of the medicine is eased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the socket to the cotton, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this repeatedly until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. And if you have to start over with the cauterization of the medicine, begin again, and after the cauterization drain the pus around the eye, using a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and treated with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective by fumigation rather than cautery; if it is treated by this method, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, gather all or some of these in one pot, put them inside, boil them; the pot should be tightly closed with strong clay, and in the pot place one instrument made of hair according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or lead, and one end should be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapors rise to the eyes through the nose, until the eye is purified; after that repeat often, until the eye dries up, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of abscess heating, for many things may happen then; do not do it except when the abscess heat is subsiding. And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and place an eggshell inside the patient's mouth so that the patient does not have too hot vapors; for the eggshell does not let the vapors weigh down on the mouth, and it is good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine is stuck in the throat, or some other thing; you must therefore pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the instrument so that you see it move; if it does not open and remains stuck in the throat, the patient must vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will expel the thing then. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and you can pull it out. And if it does not come out as we have said, take one instrument made of reed according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And bend the instruments slightly at the head so that they can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, for it may swell up or push the bone in; it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because they will move or adjust what needs to be adjusted; if they push downwards, pull it back evenly along the entire instrument until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat's cavity
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes medicine is the cavity of the throat, as I said in the division, through the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the sick person's throat towards the sun, then press their tongue to the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the cavity, pull it out with a small hook or subtle tweezers suitable for this purpose. If this is not effective, take a curved cane, and push it into the sick person's throat, then thrust or bend the end of the cane with a hot iron and repeat this often. Dip the sick person in cold water all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, open their mouth, pour it into their mouth without swallowing, and move it around with your hand frequently; and as soon as you feel the cavity, let them vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then you should sedate the patient with aphrodisiac, at the instrument I mentioned in the treatment of the eye; do this multiple times, for it will persist. The manner of the treatment is that you take one pot or one having charcoal inside, and cover it with a perforated cloth; place the head of the instrument inside it; then pour your fumigation, and have the patient place the head of the tube in their mouth, and close the mouth, so that no smoke escapes, but comes only as far as the nose; and the nasal cavity will now persist, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation multiple times; allow the patient to be thirsty, eat salty and bitter foods, and drink nothing of water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out under this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the nasal cavity, when it can be seen, resembles curved pincers for insertion into the throat; and has the appearance of a syringe tip, and is coated with lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many things resembling abscess are mentioned in this chapter, as memory recalls from one and another in this book, and they are different in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that one is similar to its likeness, and of that which contains moisture. And the second way is for the joints that are on the body. For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of the shoulder blade are different from those that occur in joints, and each should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if the abscess is not to be pierced, let it be allowed to ripen according to its completion; and if there are those that need to be pierced when they have become hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses which occur near joints. For when an abscess occurs near a joint, and is left until it has been surrounded, the ligament and nerve of the joint may rot, causing contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is from the principal member, and the piercing is delayed until it has ripened, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, and the piercing is done before it has ripened, it should not be pierced without digestion being completed, except for that which is from the foundation, which cannot penetrate fully, and be elongated inside, and a fistula forms; and it will not heal within a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess that has ripened according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the disappearance of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the swelling and opening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you should make sure the piercing is as far from the abscess as possible, and where it has opened; and let the piercing be along the length of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or near joints, nerves, and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no hair.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those who are ill, it is to be performed according to the affected member. And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion complete, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body will bleed out and it will fill with much pus; and possibly harden the lips and deepen it inside. And for any abscess which are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb requires. It is necessary that you bring small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if it has such abscesses where the care is required, and covering; when it has become as cloth, and softened, it is necessary to do as with babies: and if there are those that are cut into four angles, and if there are those from which you cover as myrtle leaf, as abscesses of the ankles; and if there are those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar punctures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When there is no head (i.e., a superficial abscess), it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in one hour, but only part of it; stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing wrongly; do this repeatedly until the pus is drained completely. This should be done with great caution when the patient is weak, such as women, children, old people or debilitated ones. Sometimes the pus may jump out with the discharge, possibly killing the patient, and you must be careful not to blame yourself. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large opening, bring linen or old cotton threads; and if it is a large abscess and there are many punctures, it is necessary that you place a thread in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut a part of the skin in the abscess and shaved it around, it is necessary to fill it with old cotton or linen gauze without moisture, and keep it for three days; then open it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and alum, wet one cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly. If the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book; and if it is winter, or the shoulder or abscess is very nervous, you must put hot tents and moistened cloths over them; and if it is summer, and the shoulder is fleshy, you must put moistened cloths on top of it, or cold water and oil, or cold water and oil cooled, for three days as we have said; then drain the abscess and treat the wound until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This is what you should know universally about the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and now here is the chapter.
des soros	on the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come in the head, there are methods that are in linens, such as the one for a bladder stone, and there are many similarities. There are some that have moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony at the base, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act against it. And the procedures of the abdomen are such that you should try all instruments called "entromissoire", from which this form follows, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, they should be done above the long one. And when the moisture is drained, scrape without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it will return immediately if left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and apply to the wound and leave until the next day; and let those who are slow-healing do this. And repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, as long as you know that it does not remain overnight; then cure the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains one hard knot, crush it along the length; throw your fingers into it, and scrape from all sides, and put all your care to draw pus out where it lies; and if the artery acts against you, do as I have told you before. And do the same for an abscess that is stony, and for removing and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a hard abscess and one with moisture is lighter, for they have little blood. And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and of those I crushed an abscess or head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a quartz stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if any had been cut into it, it would have made a wound like that of a quartz. In other abscesses coming from heads, especially those that come from children's heads and the roots of ears, they should be opened wide for as long as possible to draw out pus; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Often this abscess occurs at the neck, under the jaw, and in groins, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body; and they are large, and are joined together. And each scrofula is specifically inside its coat, as the lump of the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant which do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see a favorable disposition in the patient, and it is similar in color to the body, and silent on all sides and does not pulsate at the neck nor the artery nor the conduit, and does not penetrate; then you should cut it above, and peel off each part, and place the two lips of the curette at the anus, if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull it slowly, and be sure to not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula or lancet too sharply, so that your hand does not slip, and do not see too far ahead, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not stop bleeding, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that coagulate blood, and hold the wound; let it be until the abscess is soothed and the wound softens and begins to drain. And when the blood has clotted, return to your work, as you should; then look for your cue if there are any small scrofulas remaining, and cut them off and clean them. If there is a large root of the scrofula in the wound, do not cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang down without causing harm; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you scrape the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you gather the two edges of the wound, and sew them now, because there is no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root, and draw pus, and sew as we have said. Those scrofulas with excess, pierce where there is a more open area; and pierce it in the same way as the one mentioned above, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply enchanting char ointment until it heals.
de squinance	In this case, "de squinance" appears to be a misspelling or variant of the term "d'escroquance," which means "from squeezing." Here is the corrected line:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke about the size of the throat, but I never saw it done in our land and it is written according to their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the throat slit called "epiglote" should be cut open; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the spur of the disease are at those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the spur, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglote, it is necessary that we cut it below four circles or three small slits across, between the circles or by the quantity of the cut of the scythe, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the throat is contracted at the incision of the epiglottis, there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	If the master is afraid, then it must extend the skin of the throat all along, then cut open the chest until it reaches the ribcage; and sever the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then close the opening, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the incision of the ribcage which jumps out due to the broken place, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where doubt of strangulation exists, bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it closed with care, then apply medications that cause pus to form until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the wings are cut off.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then you tie the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it has passed in 3 days or 4.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	Then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young lady took one knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to cure it, but I found it as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and I knew that it had not opened or led to any vein other than the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly closed the wound and cured it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	The girl's voice returned to normal, and she resumed her usual condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Because I say to you that there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat   (The word 'gorge' can also mean 'throat' or 'neck', but here it refers to 'large throat' as a translation of 'la tailleure de l’epiglotte'. In modern French, 'tailleure' would not be used this way.)
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "gorge hernia", and it is a large abscess of a reddish-yellow color, and it is very common in women;   (Here, 'cist' refers to the abscess mentioned at the beginning of the line.)
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it occurs in two ways: natural or accidental; or it is not caused by an instrument.   (Here, 'et' means 'and', and the first 'ou' means 'or'. The phrase 'natureil n’a point d’engien' can be translated as 'natural has no tool', meaning that in this case, there is no external cause to the abscess.)
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents occur in two ways, one of which resembles fatty tissue and the other resembles an abscess that comes from us due to arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there should be fear and it is not good to make large incisions except in the small one, and prove it and search for the entire insertion.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you prove it like a fat lump and it does not open at all, strike it, as we do with lumps, and draw out its entire coat, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And carefully examine it completely, and treat it as appropriate, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods of ours there are, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must say all the difference between dislocation and protrusion.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Issue is heat and sustained fever while the inflammation has passed, and the swelling is complete; then the fever subsides and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With not there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains one swelling, which is its own sac and is the same color as the body, and begins like a bladder and grows larger.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to two types, either fatty or moist, and many of them are of the same color as I said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you must first test and examine all the instruments called "introscope", according to their shape that appears in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	The method of inquiry into abscesses for us is that you take the moistest place you find within the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little until you feel that the instrument has penetrated the core. Then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then straighten the dislocated joint, and beware that it does not jump out again.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the tumor runs cold, have it bled as I said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if the dislocated joint does not bring forth moisture (it is fat), make a cross-shaped incision in it, take hold of it with the pincers, and remove the skin gently from both sides, and draw the coat or membrane that covers it out along with the fat.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it whole, then draw it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if something remains, then it returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if a little remains and does not cause you grief, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, press the wound, place warm soothing things on it, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If the wound is large, cut it in two lips, and treat it with whatever that cures flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or something else, and you are forced to act quickly, use vitriol powder, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound heals, and let the swelling of the blood subside; then cover again what has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the trepan tools, and they are in three types: large, medium, and small; and among them there are four square ones called "albarets", and one called "breb", and there are also three types for encircling abscesses with fistula: large, medium, and small.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like needles used to sew charms, made of citron wood, iron, or silver; the ones colored yellow are worth more, and those with black planks are sharper for encircling abscesses with fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wound's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of tumors are much alike, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are also tumors with two curvatures in three ways.  Here comes the next sentence to translate:
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And there are also tumors with three curvatures, and these can be in four ways; and there are tumors with two curvatures as well as those with a single curvature, and they are all necessary in their place. Here is the next sentence to translate:
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these [parts] which are being cut is sharp, and those who do not cut thoroughly from one side, from where the nerves are scraped, since the vein or nerve is not struck.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these incisions are the joints tied together with stitches, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and are of four types: large, small, medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And one should not use it anywhere except in charnu (charred or burned) limbs such as legs, arms, breasts, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	Sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling plasters of fistula, in this form, for drawing blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place that bleeds from the veins and arteries, and sometimes it is reapplied in this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men become swollen when they start to decay, until they resemble the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, it must be done according to this form as described in the following lines (b) up to line (g):
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then, scrape the fat, apply the wound with a healing ointment, then bring together the two edges of the wound to stitch, and heal it until it is healed:
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	if the breast tilts downwards and is swollen due to its size as it happens with women, if so, make two slits above, by two similar incisions:
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From this, one should hold the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the .ij. lips, and remove the fat, and bring what we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it fester until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole boil that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and dress it with ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	If the abscess resembles scrofula, make incisions as we have said in the treatment of scrofula; and if the wound becomes boil-like again, bring fire as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin over it is sewn, there are often abscesses, and this also happens at an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is recognized thus, when it is for the artery, the abscesses are long in full growth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, it feels constricted; and when it is for the vein, it feels hot to the touch.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolishness to cover the abscess, especially when it is under the joints and angles and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.

In the one whose artery is swollen, an incision should be made through the skin along its length.

puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then the joint that is between the two ligaments of an incision should be held in place as long as it is not issued, and abscesses should be opened;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that binds a splint, as long as the ligament cries out;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then anoint this with ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the opening of the vein, then you should anoint your hand with it as far as the skin from the abscess;

puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Tie the abscess, as I told you, or a linen of one part to two cheeks with thread.

des apostemes des ners	from the black abscesses
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses appear in black areas when they are wounded, or due to excessive labor, and similar things.

et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is squeezed, the patient feels pain, but not all over the body, but rather under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	It should be tightly bound from all sides, and it should not move forward or backward, nor up or down. et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is either the head or forehead, should apply the spatula to the skin.

des grosses boces pendans	Large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; and there are small and very large ones.

si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart. quant li boude ist fuer	When the thigh is pierced

dou chancre	The translation is "on a boil" or "a boil".
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre originates in the marriage, and great caution is required in its cure, and the ancients stated that when chancres are in a place where it can be shaved like chancre that is on the genitals, and in the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it first appears; and when it is large and old, it is not advisable to approach it, for I never knew anyone to heal it; no one ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him sweat if there is manifest repletion, then shave the patient.i. one good place to perform the operation; then pour boiling oil or vinegar over the place where the operation will be performed; then press your thumbs or an instrument onto the chancre, and remove all of it without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely, and be careful not to prevent the bleeding by cutting into an artery or a vein, if that happens, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then treat with another remedy until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division, the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is done with medicines, and that which is cured by fire: it is only eclites; one should not touch iron in these two similarities, namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not work, look to see if the patient is weak or has other diseases besides dropsy, such as abdominal bloating and similar things; one should not touch iron in this case because there is doubt. If you see the patient strong and healthy, and he only has dropsy and nothing else, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work like this:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lay the patient straight on your hands, and let the assistant press the abdomen towards the bottom of the bladder, then take the spatula sharp pointed as shown in this form: And it should be cut into two parts with a point, but not so deep that it can reach the intestine when pushed in, and it cannot pierce through.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look to see if the dropsy is adhering towards the intestines: If it is, you must make an incision beneath the bladder 4 fingers straight downwards above the fist; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the bladder 4 fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right side, and do not let the patient lie over the incision so that the waste does not flow to that weak place.

On one side, there are three holes; on two sides, two holes, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when they trim a quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	The salve is above, so when the instrument reaches the water, press down on it now. Perform this procedure every day and avoid overindulging in food or drink except a little water.
