de l’estopement de la verge	Stopping (or treating) the member (or penis).
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	There are no children born without foreskin or whose foreskins are small or not in their proper place. It is necessary to perform circumcision immediately using a very thin spatula according to this form: then place the foreskin, which should be very thin and soft, with the tip touching the glans; tie it with a thread for 2 or 4 days until the child wants to urinate, at which point the threads are removed and urination occurs, and then the foreskin is repositioned. In case of difficulty, there is no need for concern because the urine that comes out does not leave the foreskin closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	The patient with a small putrid sore is to be treated with the plaster of pitch, as previously stated, and it will spread. Those who do not have the sore in its place are blessed, for no one is born with the sore at the head of the penis, thus they cannot urinate before raising their penis; and they cannot ejaculate due to the fact that the matter cannot reach the marris (urethra), and it is a harmful disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of work is that the patient lies on their back with the head of the penis and the buttocks aligned as the tail of a feather, so that the sore opens in the middle, as necessary; and you should beware of the flow of blood which comes often, and if it happens, you should stop the bleeding by applying pressure to the bleeding area and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	genital ulcers
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albathe comes in the penis, and it is an appearance of a bad genital condition; and there are both harmful and harmless ones; you must take them one time with very subtle hands, crush and clean all, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on top, and cure it with diafinicon ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the albathe is harmful, with a putrid color and odor, then you must apply cautery to it. When you have crushed it, and if the albathe is inside the penis and has both parts within the flesh and parts outside, then you must remove the internal albathe first; and when it is separated, cure the external part. For when you treat them together, there is no certainty that the genitals will not be perforated, and blackness and corruption come into the penis and surrounding area; you must clean all that is black and corrupted, then lay ointment made of pomegranate rind and honey on top, and cure it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery as follows: The cautery helps with two conditions at once: bleeding and corruption. If the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert or guide a tube made of wood from the plum tree into the penis, and make the patient urinate; when the hair reaches the tip of the penis (which is for those who have not been circumcised), if it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you must shave with one instrument, removing all the skin until the ligaments are released, and liberate the penis from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is serious to discuss this, you should cauterize it with a small spatula about half an inch from the tip of the vein and the skin; then press gently between 2 fingers, and put a thin linen cloth dampened with cold water on it, so that it does not immediately come away.
de la circoncision	When performing circumcision, first cleanse the member completely with warm water; then take a sharp knife and cut off the foreskin, leaving a little skin at the bottom.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not without its complications, like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will and for infants, it is necessary that we do the best job possible and make it as easy as possible for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	I wanted the greater part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision to have at least one dagger, and with force, and in all one novacula; but the cowardly ones fled because there are two layers, and by chance if he strikes the upper one and delays the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it is covered and the pain is doubled, and at the mundification which is done with a dagger, the tip of the member is not secure; and in the mundification of the nail, by chance the iron escapes and spoils the work, and many times are born like that which do not need mundification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding the amputation that is made to all the links of the chain, I have found the advantage in the experiment, because the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, the links are equally shortened all the time, but ensure that the wires are tightly closed around the skin, and use the method of the first work so that you make the child think that you are not forcing him to tie the wire only around the rod, but then let him go in every way possible.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make the child place his hands straight in front of him and keep the forces hidden behind your hands or under your feet so that the children do not see them, nor any instruments; then bring your hand to the rod and blow or call out, and pull it up until the head of the rod is immersed; then clean the area well of the filth assembled there, then tie a double stitch at the join, then tie one link to another at each interval; hold the second stitch by the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two links, then tie the wire quickly and pull the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the pus flow drop by drop, for it is the humors; and put powder on top and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with a mixture of cooked egg white tempered with rose water, boiled with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and heal it with other treatment until it becomes healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The forms of the forces for the healing are as follows: the two cheeks should be tender and thin, and the cheeks should also be as wide as the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the healing is when the kernels are at incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, so that the lesion becomes an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days and what is beneath the scrotum is swollen, leave it until the abscesses have subsided and gently scrape it; if it bursts as you can move it, be careful of the part of the scrotum, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the affected area with powder on a shallow wound as we have said about treating powders, and if it bursts excessively and goes above, this will not harm anything; heal it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or blood congealed, or pus, or frozen meat, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine is not relieved and you see that it is retained due to a stone in the bladder or urethra, then the patient should be bent over their knees; their feet should be placed on the back, and their abdomen from the upper part of the back should be extended, and the patient should be restrained as much as possible; then the collector's gloves should be used to forcefully express the stone above the bladder, so that the urine is relieved.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," of which this is its form: it should be made of thin silver, light and slender like a bird's feather; it should have a tube of about half a palm in length, and it should be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the discharge of urine is that you take one double thread, tie one end to the head, one piece of wool or cotton, and push the head into the syringe; and stop the excess of the linen and push it up to the head of the syringe, then oil or butter and egg yolk anoint the syringe, and make the patient sit on a chair, and rub the bladder and penis with moist oil of olive and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis over the anus; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel it come to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then the thread follows the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the thread, then pull out the thread forcefully, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	The diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is assembled there, and you see it distill acids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydra", and its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and it has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the upper end has a cap so that the medicine can flow out in such a way that it stops the urine without adding anything, if possible to draw out the moisture, and push when needed;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see to throw your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the cuke in the moisture, and draw it along which is within; if you draw out the moisture with the cuke, and then forcefully push the cuke along; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which the bladder is cleansed: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is raised one hand's breadth or the size of the links. Then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you wish to cleanse the bladder with. Then tie this between two hands using a good double thread, and heat one end of the moisture over the fire. Then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then hold your hand under the bladder with all the moisture coming towards it, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like a pouch and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press firmly with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction with medicines; and I have said the difference between the embedded stone in the intestine, and all the signs, and when you should work on a stone of size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often with children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it opens the urinary orifice, it inflames the patient's penis, it pricks it many times, then binds it; and the jumping of these stones often causes foundation problems; and the healing of children is light until they are 4 years old, and it is severe in adults, and it is most moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the feces that are in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders seeking for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and tilt him downwards and move him, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and rises a little towards the top; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then press it and touch it from within.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the cavity, hurry up and cut into the stone above it. And if it does not fall out by touching it all over, moisten your left thumb if the patient is an infant, or moisturize your little finger, if the patient is a young adult completed; and push it to its base, try to remove the stone, when you feel it in your hand, press it against the bladder opening; then press on it and push it towards the place where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press on the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to stretch out his right hand above, and remove the skin that is under the bladder in the part where you make the incision; then push the spatula covering it, so it takes its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make the incision between what is between the ureters and the base, not at the middle but along the left side of the navel; and it should be straight above the stone, and your hands should be at its base or in its middle, and it should be cut through so that it is wide on the outside and narrow on the inside, according to the size of the stone, but not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure that is its foundation, must jump without any effort; and know that there is this stone or it has angles and edges; it is necessary to extract it; and if it is soft, like a plum pit, and rounded, where the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Then in the place that has angles and edges, make a larger incision; and if it does not jump out, then you must forcefully extract it using pliers shaped like a limer at the end, to press the stone so that it does not escape; or you can push underneath it with a thin curved instrument at the end; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, enlarge .1 inch hole and remove without cortex, then stretch it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, push the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then pound it, pull it out, and take out the smaller ones afterwards. If they are very large, they must be cut into pieces and make a larger incision. For the patient has two outcomes: he dies, or urine comes out immediately because the bladder cannot be sealed; but still try to extract or break apart with pliers until you remove it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, tighten it, and put a moist, oiled cloth on top; or in oil and cold water, or rosewater and cold water, to soothe the abscess heat; then make the patient lie down on their neck, and do not loosen the ligament until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you loosen it, rinse well the area with oil and water, then apply healing ointments such as diaphanicon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If an abscess or corruption comes up in the wound and if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is retained which is known to be harmful without its release: then press your thumb on the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause injury.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then clean the wound that is deep and shallow and inflamed, and help in all ways you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that every herb you use to treat him, you bind his thighs with them and apply the medicine on its place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is guided by a rod and pierced and urine cannot pass out of it; treat it in this way, you cut it many times until the passage is opened, it is excused from cutting due to this treatment. I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a metal probe of this shape and sharp at four angles pierced into one thread:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	1. Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft of the stone under the bladder, so that it does not return to the bladder.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason preventing it, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the lower thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from a woman's stone (ovary)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens rarely that a stone is in the womb of women, and if it ever happens, it is a great grief for the cure, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a woman skilled enough who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in the woman's body is deeper than the stone in a man, which means it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need to do this (remove the stone), then it is necessary that you take a skilled midwife and at all costs find her, and if you cannot find one, not even a chaste virgin; and present a wise woman in the art of women's lives or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do what you command for the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And carefully examine whether the woman is a virgin; then you must push her vagina or foundation and search for the stone; if you find it, force it below her vagina, and advise her to push with her hand where the patient is, and press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If you find it (the stone), she should move it little by little from the bladder opening towards the root of the thigh until it reaches the root of the cuntis; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh near the mule with the con, where it is moved and feels the stone in that area; do not move her hand above or below the stone, and let it be cut into small pieces.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the root towards the thigh, if you feel the stone so that the wound opens enough for the stone to come out; know that there are many types of stones: small and large, smooth and rough, long and round, and those with veins. Know their appearances to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone protrudes, place vitriol powder on it and hold for an hour until the bone is set; then return to your work, until the pain subsides, and have the tools I told you about in the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the bone protrudes and it is an artery that is cut, place powder on the wound and apply tight bandages and do not continue, let the arrowhead remain and do not draw it out for fear of killing the patient; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is alleviated and the wounds are healed, return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of a flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A hernia aquosa is nothing but an accumulation of moisture or white matter, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called a "white matter," and sometimes it is specifically in the egg's lining, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not occur without pain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the bladder, and this moisture has many colors: either it turns yellowish, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is completely white as we have said, it is an abscess, that is, long like an egg, and the eyes do not open, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very cloth, it is an abscess with part of the egg and because of this, one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the eyes and the white part that is completely white, one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe thoroughly with a blunt instrument, so that the shape is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the intruder, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be anesthetized to our power and the filling of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a little high, and put many layers of cloth underneath him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then lie him on his left side, and command the assistant to lie on his right, and extend the staff between one of the two joints of the hips.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula and strike the hide of the hocks through its length up to the heel, and make your incision straight in dividing the hide of the hocks as far as the white tendon, and peel off the skin carefully according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the white tendon with sharp needles about one finger's breadth wide and draw out all the liquid, then place your thumbs, and stretch the white tendon upward; do not touch the bone of the hock, but only the white tendon; strike all around it carefully or in pieces, for if you don't strike it well, the liquid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the calf jumps away from your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work with the white tendon; then bring together the two sides of the bone of the hock with a stitch, then treat it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted with another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; afterwards strike the coccyx to the whole suspension, and extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the egg is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; strike the other part similarly as you did the first, then squeeze out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put more moistened linen in wine and oil, and place them on the coccyxes, and cover it with double cloths, and tie it above all the cord that is according to this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two bandages, and make them of linen cloth in this manner and sew them together in the belt of the breeches, and one of the heads takes hold beneath the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the fist; and the other two heads above the two angles, and let all the rest be gathered together in the loop of the belt.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramice of cautery is used in place of iron surgery, and you take one cautery scalpel and cut the skin of the boils, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the water is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this form and pierce the boil with it, and peel off this thin layer of skin using the hot and sharp cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cup in all ways you can, as long as you are heating it; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and beware of the disorder of blood, and be cautious about the surgeries of cutting.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything happens contrary to it, or abscess swelling or bleeding or something else, if you cure what is happening contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	and if the patient is afraid and does not want to wait for this work due to its horror, then bring a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have said that the water has been brought out,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part beneath all the spittle wide, and make the perforation long along the body; and let the holes be large, so that all the pus flows out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and let the remaining pus flow out, then heal it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white linen cloth does not allow the pus to come out of the wound's mouth, then you must put a pen or instrument for draining pus from dropsy in it, as its shape is shown before; and widen one side of the wound slightly, feel that the pus returns, and collect it after 6 months or so, and when it is collected as described before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	From the abscess of the eyes
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the case of this operation, there are many possible positions due to which it seems to me that one should remain still.

Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, including the eyes; and it is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known by excessive sharp and hot, which is spread on the kidneys, or through beating;

et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance it is a swollen and hard abscess, and of that color, and sometimes comes from an artery, or from the inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers;    Quant c’est de enflure de voine, si est conus par la doulour qui vient des parties sus et dedens, et par li est mueve et se moult agrandit.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	One who is afflicted with inflammation of the vein is known by the expression of the touch of the fingers.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of an abscess of the eyes
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is a swelling resembling a boil on the eyelids, with softening of the eyes  (eyelids)

de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the vein
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The results of this procedure are due to the section that comes or the breaking of the vein, or the extension onto the abdomen in the area of the inguinal region, because the intestines descend from that opening to one of the cavities.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this wound is either shallow or deep, and it comes in these two ways of causing injury: either by impact, or by jumping, or by twisting, or by lifting a heavy weight, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of the shallow wound are that they happen gradually, over a long time, and do not come suddenly.

puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then heal the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a hinge which joins together the bone, in this manner you bind the joints, after the cut lightly above them.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then insert it into the wound and treat the abscess of those who open it, until the joints fall apart; and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there comes gangrene within wounds, as we have said, and open the joints; do not remove any intestines from the anus, and if some are removed, it is bad, and repair them hourly.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And if it remains too long at this point, the wound or abscess believes that the intestines are descending.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	This happens by the extension of the abscess, which is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then the muscles and ligaments become softened and opened up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then strike the place of the rupture swollen with a blow of a distance of 3 fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then draw out the pus that is under the skin which lies beneath, then take the rod and place it on the apparent place of the pus;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press with the entire abdomen, then cut the two apparent places of the pus on the head of the rod, and do the same for both sides;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the rod and do not cover or extend the pus or any other thing, as I have informed you in the treatment of the removal of the entrails;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then heal by the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the threads, if it bleeds and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The leech is confined and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is heated up in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the heels
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the heels becomes soft in some men, because the fat inside is softened and can be seen; when it is observed that it needs to be cured, one should make the patient lie on their back, and cut the softened skin above the natural skin; then assemble two lips together for a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess skin of the softened area with 2 or 4 firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and heal as other wounds do, until it is healed, and cut the threads.
dou chastrement	The torture
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The use of torture is mentioned in our law, and I would prefer not to discuss it in this book; however, it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the mirrors answer when asked about it, as well as its remedy; and the other, because we often need to torture animals to help us, such as sheep, goats, cattle, and other animals. Therefore, I say that torture is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the method of attraction, we place the animal in hot water until the skin is softened and relaxed; then we grab it with our hand, making sure it is held firmly so that it does not move anymore. As for the method of cutting, first we mark the animal, then we press the skin of its anus with our left hand, tie it up, and strike above each testicle once or twice depending on how thoroughly we have scorched them; leave a small amount of pus and the subtle pus that is over the vessels; this method of torture differs from that by attraction because sometimes something remains in the anus due to attraction, causing the animal to desire pleasure; then cure the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	1. Hermaphrodite is according to .ij. forms in humans: one of which is between the two openings, as the figure of nature for a woman, who has hair, and sometimes urinates from it.  And the other form is in women, and has on top of the penis like a rod and two openings.  And the treatment of both man and woman is that you cut around the adjacent areas entirely, and treat them as other wounds; in the second form, in men whose urine jumps from the skin of the openings, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	The disease or illness:
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	de la tentigene:
de erratique	From erratic [situations]
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	In erratic [situations], the nature of a woman is not understood, or the opening is small; it can be natural by birth, or an accident caused by illness that comes upon it; or it can be due to incorrect positioning, or from a subtle or thick siphon, and it occurs either in marriage or during childbirth, or during labor, or after; and one must avoid conceiving, and the delivery, and unfortunately causing the flowers to bloom; and the recognition of these is by the observation of the belly. If the opening appears close, whether at your fingers or the eye [vulva], you hasten, and press in this manner: put your fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spread out her legs; then form the two openings, until the subtle siphon is round, and the opening is closed; then take linen and moisten it with oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman rest for each day so that it cannot heal. And if the siphon is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula resembling a mirte leaf. If the opening is from a tear, suspend it at the onyx [urethra] and cut; and have ready medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together in abundance of egg; then bring a wide plank, so that the wound cannot heal; and let it be long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then heal other wounds until it is healed. And when in childbirth there is a tear, it must be covered according to this manner, unless it is an abscess that has been festered. For the festered abscess that is in childbirth, one must not touch to heal.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids [a condition characterized by inflammation of the veins around the anus or lower rectum]
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. "Emorroydes are openings of veins which without care usually heal on their own." - Emorroidas son las aberturas de venas, las cuales sin atención usualmente sanan por sí mismas.
des apostemes de la marris	"from the rectum" - del recto
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many methods of abscess come in the marriage (the body), such as carbuncles, pus-filled abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatise the abscess that comes in the marriage, which is not one of those abscesses that cling together; and if you want to know the work with fire, observe whether the abscess is agitated at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red which you can see.  Then do not rush to pierce, but let it heal until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on one seat, and he should have two small seats or he leans, and support his back and assemble his feet at the parts away from the leg; and his legs should be spread out, and place his arms under his thighs, and tie them well with a strong ligament; then bring the pus to the left side of the abscess, and introduce the instrument used to open the abscess cavity, which will follow the shape; and when you introduce this instrument, ensure that it does not penetrate too deep into the abscess, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is large, cover the depth of the abscess with cloths so that the instrument does not harm it; and place the mouthpiece of the instrument on top, and mark the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one can feel it with the hand, it should be covered with a linen cloth dipped in oil or rose oil; and put the cloth over the abscess and over the handle linen cloth that is clean and moistened with water or medicinal herbs that are cooked; then cover it for two days with ointment until it heals; and sometimes lift the abscess and the wound by applying a cloth dipped in water and honey, and then apply water or long-cooked herbal remedies such as lily root and aristolochia; then return to the ointment.  And if the wound closes again in the abscess, you must be careful not to burn with fire, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	The birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the shape of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see a woman push downwards, and desire to urinate; then the child should hasten to be born. So, know that this delivery is according to natural shape, and it is the head of the child that comes out first, followed by the second part with it. When you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on the woman's abdomen so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends towards the head, the second part follows, and the husband is cleansed of his waste by good cleansing. And he who comes in another way does not come naturally. For sometimes he comes from his feet, or the body or limbs come, or the hands, or he comes to the abdomen or chest, or he may be turned around accidentally on his neck, and in other evil shapes; it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and skilled in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out first through natural delivery and the woman delivers with great effort, and her strength is weak, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the midwife's little spatula between her fingers in the shape shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the second part, and strike it with its nails until the membranes that are inside come out; and hold the woman's belly as the child descends, and if it does not descend, you should cleans her privates with mustard oil of fenugreek; then make her take a position and vomit, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour; this will now bring forth the child. And if two hands come out first, you should gently pull them back bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, have the woman sit on one saddle, and lift her feet up; then tilt the saddle onto the ground, and anoint the woman so that she does not urinate when tilting; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child is dead, strike its hands with the knife shown above and extract the child, and pull it out gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	The issue of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes upon his feet, you must push him upward.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn the feet this way and that, until they are even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one of the feet and stretch it out this way and that.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump up to any kidneys, if commanded to catch it, and make it vomit by means of a concoction;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it leaps (the condition), if God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not leap as we have said, you must turn it gently and slowly, according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, take musk-powder from high places, oil of rosin, melted gum, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and place the nature of the woman within it and drive this ointment out.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in a cold bath up to her chest;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when it is softened inside, make one myrrh collier and put it beneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make it sit on a chair, then make it vomit and hold its mouth and nose shut, and gently press the abdomen, for the child now jumps (or moves restlessly).
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the exit of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When a child comes in this form, put the balm on their hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then lay it on its neck, and let the feet hang downwards, and let it lie on one bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend its hands little by little, then bind the hands above the belly, and open the cushions underneath until it is prepared below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	if the child does not jump, take its feet and bend them forward, then bend the belly upwards, and put your hands inside.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And rock the child gently, and instruct the woman to take care until the infant issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the infant's delivery which comes out with a hand's breadth wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then raise the woman and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot walk, make it lie down on a bed, and bend its legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the mustard plaster as I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it does not give birth, make it sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and help the baby according to its natural shape, and make it vomit, and command it to grasp as tightly as possible until the afterbirth issues forth;
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the birth of the child on its neck, and it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	The bailiff should touch his hand, then turn it little by little and pull gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, place natural mucilage of high altitude and oil on it, as we have said, then instruct it to move a little at a time;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make it sit on a seat, and instruct it to hold itself; and make it vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, you should proceed with everything
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	Press it in this manner for everything, grasp the dislocation with your nail until all moisture is gone.

adonques si istra legierement.	Then ease it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins

de plusors enfans	of many children (lit. from many children)
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Never are formed in marriage (lit. de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
