pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take the defined ointment, and make it with rose oil and an equal part of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; and the same is more effective when heated and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When the diaphysis (long bone shaft) is absent,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them into powder, and sprinkle it on honey when it is above the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then stretch one cloth over it and place it on his chest, and sometimes an Aristotle's long needle is administered,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And roots of this celestial [substance], which is as fine as flour and chalk.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And in the use of simple [medicines] or composites: grind them, make powder, mix with the honey I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	If the wound is long and not treated by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Therefore know that corruption arises fully, and causes impression in the bone, or in hard members, or ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If you treat the treatment of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaric is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or the foot, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed, and no care is taken, one abscess swells up.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they will cut and throw down the toe as far as it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may be cut completely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the rot reaches the bone as far as there is a foul smell, and the foot becomes wide and swollen, and the color changes.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Then it is necessary that you remove all the superfluous part that remains of the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail follows the flesh closely, and it begins to swell, and bleed.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put the medicine under the nail so as not to damage the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and press it gently and lightly on top,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And place on top of it the remaining part of the charmed medicine, burning and corrosive, to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure with herbs until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, strike it and draw it out, because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth become corrupt, strike it in one of its roots as mentioned before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal while it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is wounded and bruised, and feels great pain, then you must first heal the wound;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then cut the nail of the spur-toe obliquely across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And warn that the incision shall not reach up to the flesh which is beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, put something on top to alleviate.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand is deafening
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The growth that arises in the hand of some men by chance is entirely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And sometimes there is bone or nail [in it], and occasionally there is a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And in some cases they grow from the root of the joint, or their growth is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that grows in any of the fingers does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and the one that grows at the joint of the finger, may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The thickness of a fat person is light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the root, with a broad spatula-like instrument.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	A newborn from the joint root is difficult to cure; hold it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In a newborn or one who was born prematurely, you must first cover the cartilage all the way to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then insert the bone into a suitable socket for it, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the joints often come by birth, or by injury from a wound, or by burn from fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you must treat the swelling, it should be treated according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two layers or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you put between two thin wooden pieces [or blocks], until the joints are joined, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it happens that one of its two [parts] comes with the palm, then strike the joiner [or joint] as necessary.
Des vils	Of villagers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, swollen, and full of melancholic fluids that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it often happens in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, more so than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer purge for the liver, and then cleanse the basilica (small intestine).
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to strike them and draw out black bile;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other method is to tie the vein, and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The thigh is to be prepared in this manner: first boil the leg with very hot water strongly, until the flesh becomes tender.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then hold the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then make an incision in one place, or two, or three, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then draw out and squeeze out black blood from your hand, from one end to the other, as much black blood as the strength of the sick person can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it and instruct him to soak himself in meats reddening dark-colored linens;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And start evacuating and healing again when the veins are full, which helps the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of it [the affected limb] is done in this way: lift the patient's leg, if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then immerse it [the affected limb] in water and let the leg be submerged in hot water until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have water, heat it over the fire, then apply it to the vein along the long part of the thigh or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with a knife, and strip the vein from both sides until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And it is seen red and black, and when it enters or skin resembles as a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then press the root beneath, until it is swollen in the skin, and then cut it obliquely light,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then strike it in another place three fingerbreadths below; then skin the skin above the vein as far as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then tie the root, as you have done, and cut it obliquely again, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take another size [of something], if necessary; then flatten it [the size], and place it on the foot of the patient.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw it out [the size] and flatten it to a second size; then cut it down gradually, until it becomes completely thin, and place it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift [the size], then push an awl with a very thick double thread into it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And pull and draw it (the dislocated joint), and push it below the right rib, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes back into place.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted out, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it (the wound), put linen soaked in vinegar and oil on the place of the wound, and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the wound is contracted, twisted, and rolled up together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you must cut it (the dislocation), do so forcefully, but do not cover it; pull it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to pierce the vein is curved and does not cut, so do not use it for opening the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curve because if it is small, it would pierce the vein; but be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to putrefaction that arises under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes within the body and turns towards the outside, vein it between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it causes a very large swelling in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the joint changes, and the vein begins to emerge, as a root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood from one and a half to two cubits long, and sew it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it comes out, you wrap it around the wood, and sew it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover the base until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	If you apply it [cautery], it enters into the flesh, brings about abscess and pus or ill health.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Because of this, it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein, when treated, is of five or ten finger-lengths long.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one honest man came to me, whose it [vein] was ten finger-lengths long, and when you apply it, press a pound or two, and pierce it all the way through.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Empty everything within it; and let the matter inside be vacated, and bring medicines for decaying pus to its place every day, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	Also, do not reopen this vein too often, especially when it opens at the joint of the arm or leg.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it comes out much pus, and it frequently reopens; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "malady of ox" in our land, because it often occurs in cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, moving upwards and downwards throughout the body,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt in one limb to another, as long as it goes under the skin or runs through it.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is infested with putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, snakes, larvae and roundworms or belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And one doubts its malice, for when it passes through the body, it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it to be cured and drained, one cannot force it unless when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	it is necessary that you tie the joint above and below with a strong and narrow ligament.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then strike above and pull hard, if the bone is turned in completely into the flesh, and you cannot feel it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you burn with fire above, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it does is that it runs the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold the cork underneath it, then strike on top and pull hard;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and the patient must use body cleansing with dissolving medicines for removing bad humors;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if they rot from eating spoiled meat.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from windiness (indigestion)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and afterwards, it rose like a worm towards the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, as live silver when it cuts from one thing to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain spread from that place and pierced into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And after a short while, it runs throughout the body until it comes to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I found that it turns around the body as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moves from limb to limb, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had often heard that pain moves from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it at all, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, such constrictive wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are fat and have moist bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you wish to treat this disease, if the patient feels that pain as we have said, if it opens as we have mentioned,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	and press above and below forcefully until the gas constraint is released to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the remedy for those who swell up with wind, similar to foul-smelling pills, serapin pills, and similar ones, is administered.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various shapes and sizes depending on where they strike the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of arrows is that some have large points, small, curved, and hinged.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have two angles, and of these who have tongues, and of those where it has parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and when a limb dislocates, it does so in two ways: either in the principal member (the head), or in the member that is not the head,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	either in the cerebellum, brain, liver, spleen, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls (the limb) into any position of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you later become apparent to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Then it is necessary for you to know the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this sign is not apparent to you at all, and the arrow is not fully in, draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes the bone and pierces through it, and a soft spot appears on the skull:
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It means:
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	"and possibly without discharge from the nostrils or ears; and possibly it affects speech and voice;"
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	"and from the wound there comes out white moisture like pus, and also as if it were boiling with heat;"
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, refrain from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces the body is that it is near the left breast and feels like it has been driven into a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, the arrow may also become numb like hair, turn black with cold blood, and bring chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, it is clear that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has never pierced the bone is when there is no pus-like scum jumping out from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed of the wound, it is lodged between the ribs; it causes great pain and heavy breathing and moves all the limbs of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow falls on the stomach, it might cause something undigested flesh to jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly, and does not burst from the intestinal passage, there is no hope in treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes into the bladder, and the urine bursts out and flows away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the hands and arms, throat, shoulder, neck, spine of the back, wrists, hips, legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, you should do this instead.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	A certain man had an arrow that fell or lodged in the root of his neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it, and drew it out through the fat of the ear from another side, and found it unharmed.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I played with an arrow that had fallen in the oil under the paper beneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was withdrawn, and could not reach its point towards the flesh.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, with very sharp iron points on both ears; the wound was clean, and no evil accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And it drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow had Arabic ears (i.e., cross-shaped barbs).
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was a barber, and sharpened it until I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow from a man who is fallen or wounded, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, loosened it, drew it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish, a man whose arrow has fallen or pierced his back, and the wound has been sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any problem in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you wish another man whose arrow has fallen into his face and the wound has been sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	It stays in this state for a long time with much suffering, and many other similar symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	Draw an arrow through the one eye of the prince's king, who was struck in the middle of the nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly slanted towards the right side; and the arrow was completely straight.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been fallen for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I took it with a fine probe and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt a pain and discomfort beneath its right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place on the swollen joint an attractant and digestive plaster, because the joint does not inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the arrow's joint appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I placed the plaster on it for several days, and healed the wound directly, and the patient remained in good condition for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow within his neck for one day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine for many hours, until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I pulled at it and felt the head of the arrow which adheres to its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed the limit beyond four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then pull apart the wound that I pierced with the pliers, and pull from both sides, and it cannot be closed.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not stop refining and inventing ways with instruments until I got it after a day with well-made pliers.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to its shape that comes at the end of this chapter, as I pierce it and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the eyes judge that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will set it (the dislocation) right then, and the wound will be healed, and the patient will recover completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	You have been told about the quality of extracting some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your care to what I am not saying because books cannot fully understand.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters understand little about much, and especially about the present and failing things.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True new work, and nine instruments, for the examination of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter the limbs where they are driven except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the flesh or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps out from there where it enters is an arrow entering the flesh, and it may jump out at some point now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is healed around it and allow the opening to close.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is embedded in bone and cannot be extracted, leave it for some days and try to extract it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And when it jumps out or does not, perforate it with a fine needle all around until the flesh is enlarged and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is driven into the bone of the head and goes to one of the brain ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned do not let it drain but leave it as long as it is equal after certain days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow reaches the heart, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow has not pierced through but only into the bone and has not reached the flesh,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient remains for several days without bad incident, unless there is an attempt to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply pierced and cannot be drawn out, administer tourniquets around it as I told you; then heal the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is placed back in the body so that it cannot be seen, probe for it thoroughly;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, pull it with any suitable tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if the wound is narrow and the arrowhead deep,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone or nerve nor vein, make the opening large enough for the wound to be wide;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	pull the arrow out if possible, and if there are ears in the arrowhead like it holds on,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone, which is fixed by 2 parts to the muscles that you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrowhead of the arrow as much as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	being careful not to break the arrow, that you may pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, push the lymph down to the joints around it, then pull it, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes it (the cautery), bring what we have said about its treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and put a device as to how you can draw out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	soon or later, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot do so, place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from elsewhere, opening anything of them, or the skin is swollen in some place as it can be seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then pierce it, holding it there until the pincers can take hold and then pull it out; if it jumps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it were of an arrow in it, push it all out;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it is dislocated, and you wish to administer a remedy for it, then administer one instrument of traction.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push harder,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is caught in the hair, push one instrument with pointed end entering in, to make easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched (wounded), it is necessary that you cut around the entire flesh where the poison is, if possible,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly, bladder, flank, or side, and it is close enough that you can cover over it, do so;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And keep from cutting the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, and then cut the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And heal it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers used to extract arrows is similar to an eagle's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the growing hair is similar to a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To push the point of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tweezers for pushing and for grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins which one heals are thirty-one, of which the head is sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: two bands that are located after the ears, they are called the "double herb."
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two apparent temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	2 veins are located within 2 eyes of the 2 eyelids, which are called "aspirates".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	The vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the nose's head.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	the 2 tendons which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the 2 veins that are in lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	2 veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly bled are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the laymen call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the laymen call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the left side.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this one from which one drains, which opens clearly above the buttocks.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The salvation vein is the one that is between the auricular and annular arteries, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot are three veins: one which is beneath the hollow of the left calf.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nese", which is in the other ankle.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The purification of veins that are located behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the purgative, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	As long as the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Find where the pulse is beneath your neck, and press there firmly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and thrust it through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	cut and the skin and the vein two fingers deep, and make the blood come out as you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold and bind it until it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, is as effective for migraines.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and softening, and the common treatment for eye diseases, and to the body of the eyes with tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient extends his neck, until two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath your thumb, and then press inward;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then raise the pressure on the vein above your thumb index, and push the lancet beneath it;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And open the vein high, and strike it (the vein), just like you did in two other veins, and make the flow of blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form a knot (to stop the bleeding) and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their dressing and extraction (of objects), where our book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth just as much as the healing of the cerebral vein in the diseases of the face that are migraines and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the qualities are such that the patient stretches their neck while twisting it until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand (or something else), and allow the blood to flow according to the amount that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healthy and never make an opening with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and the vein must be crossed, for the bone is close by, and in case of an accident, the flames might break it when they are too fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The veins of the two arms aid the eyes, and the thigh, and the ankle, and the urine in oil, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their blood is such that the patient stretches their neck in twisting by some rope, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then, let the blood be healthy and the vein should be long, about a finger-width wide, for there is no heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the vein is thin, it may break; then correct the blood flow, as needed, and then tie it up with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the neck is useful for scabies, syphilis, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If it comes like an inflammation and reddening that appears in the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the characteristics of the pus are such that the patient strangles himself with his neck, then strains his genitals with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and stick it into the space between the two nostrils;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well in that way, and the pus will soon start to spread;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep [into the body], and correct the blood flow as necessary, then leave it for a night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the shape of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of two glands helps in the setting of the fracture, and at the beginning of healing, and for many diseases, and to heal ulcers, and to stop putrefaction, and sores, and scrofula.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the salve is that the patient lowers their neck beneath both of them, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master stand above the sick person, and the sick person sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein along its length with a small incision, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then tie off the other vein, untie the ligature, and squeeze the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient must not strain himself; leave him until morning so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	On the healing of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of mouth wounds assists in the cooling of the mouth and the corruption of gums, as well as cuts and swellings of the lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the jaw, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right cheek and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Take both of them then, and if you do not recognize them, and you have doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you take the larger one of each pair, and do the same for the two veins that are mentioned above, as it is the same in both cases.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the saliva beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The saliva that is in the veins beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic salivation, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of saliva are that the patient should sit with their hands in front of the sun, lift the tongue, and look down at each side to see a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore, one on both sides, but do not go too deep, for beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins from which one commonly heals are usually healed according to two methods: [or "The veins that are commonly healed are done so by two methods:"]
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or pricking entirely with a large flame of myrtle or subtle olive oil as you know to cauterize, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirteenth is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It has need to be used for opening large veins that contain much apparent blood and are troubled;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and it is for healing subtle veins with thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cure of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are under the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the master to heal properly, and he should drain the artery that is underneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then it must be stopped as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pricked, but cut as a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the abscess does not open clearly, you must force it open and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want any drain from it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and stop the flame with a nail, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the joint, then it is also necessary that you dislocate the arm and touch the joint until you recognize the pulses;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location with a pen, and then bind the arm, and burn the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware not to cut into the artery when you see the location swelling, for that is the artery; remove it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding upwards like a child's urine and the area is red and delicate, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry up then, and place your hand upon it for a long time, afterwards break your hand without cutting, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie the arm and leave it like that, do not let the patient move it; and be careful, do not let him move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not bleeding and the medicine is not present, and it swells up, then cut open the artery if it is open, because the head will shrink back; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fir bark, cut it, take one half and tie it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it bleeds, that's fine; if not, treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding is not always necessary in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the ligament on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps treat blood from the head above, and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalica, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the master to dig deep for the nerve that is beneath, and if it pricks too far through, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and inflates it and the patient grows weaker, and in some cases cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument anesthetic; and cut the nerve as much as your power allows.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sandbag of the head helps, pulling blood from the head and assisting the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to sandbag while pricking with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, as there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Therefore, one must seek out the lighter joint, and not worry if it is necessary to try the first time, and then continue.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And in some men, joints swell up, which requires the first attempt, but do not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is only done for the preservation of health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid coming diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the vein should be opened in one of the four places where it is available: namely, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	it should be opened at the beginning of spring, in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	it should be opened on the first or third day, after two or four hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine given for diseases has no fixed hour, but when needed, day or night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to treat children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman in labor except during the fourth or fifth month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to be treated, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that the intestines are cleansed with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If much feces are retained, so that the veins do not expel the waste products harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor let the one who is excessively salted with meats, or drunk, vomit, nor those who are uric.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one is purged after a colic illness, vomiting, abdominal distention, repeated copulation, overwork, staying up late, and fasting, or when the power has been completely exhausted, or by something related to the weapon or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly balance the humors, if it lacks size, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have that power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then, unless anything prevents it, into a bath for the purpose of subtly thinning the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein with the disease outside of the third part, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day from work, pain, lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be tied and raised, and let the healer's hands be higher than those who are being treated, and rub the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then carefully extract the thread, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct itself.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the healer's hands with a little bit of old oil, then place your right hand's thumb on the vein beneath the area you want to treat.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	That the vein does not break and fail when piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which run like cords to strain, and some of them are filled with pus.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Therefore, when fire is applied, it pulls away from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, therefore, the surgeons should be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then continue a little below or above that place where it did not open, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the patient fears and the place is swollen, let it rest for one or two days and do not tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case abscesses come up, do not enter (or touch) them with water, but start the healing process if it pleases the patient.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the perforation is small or shallow and you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, put the flame directly on the perforation itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Widen the opening slightly, so that the flesh swells; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh swollen, do not begin sewing immediately, and put a little lard oil on it, for it will cleanse the wound of blood, and the lard oil will solidify in that place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And so administer the oil of linseed to each wound that you open a vein, for stopping the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And likewise apply treacle and poultice to them when they are placed on the wound; thin it and spread it if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	If an abscess becomes large, which often happens when the wound is not opened sufficiently,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put a damp sponge soaked in vinegar and warm water on it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you must do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it stays in its place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not matter.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh inside a hot poultice, plaster, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica: put your hand on it then, and if you find it soft with the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put anything on top of what has been said, for by chance it may be in court without the artery; but make .i. plug (or pressure) dry to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its power, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, allow it to drain until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, allow it to become subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are full and hollow, and need extraction of blood, it should be made a larger wound, and the veins wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it should be drained little by little, and it must be drained by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of draining is safe from corruption of blood and compression of nerves, and it is more beneficial than long draining rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the body needing to drain, it is necessary to give moistened bread at the bottom of quince pits; if it is heated, let it draw blood four or five times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold constitution, give it moist bread softened in syrup made from honey or scented syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cardamom, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	If it is swollen, after the issue of blood, you should give him broth of meat and fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood from the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if you wish to shatter some bone [or break a bone], and heal it again later, as necessary, when it has been weakened by long healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If you wish to shatter some bone [or break a bone] after the first healing, and it has been strong, it should heal in 9 hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If you wish to heal from another side, it should heal on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body which is already overheated, and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw a large quantity of blood, and open the vein until it gushes.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you should treat all conditions of health, and place your hand on top of the pulse when it is healthy, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not good that when you dislocate the arm, and draw blood a second time, and the wounds are closed, that you push forcefully.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is curved, that you extend the arm as far as possible, for it would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it [the wound] bleed a second time; or you prick with the tip of the flame until the congealed blood from the vein flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And place on it, i.e., a piece of linen soaked in hot water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the abscess has burst, leave it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If you need to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or in another vein or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is connected to the carotid artery because it is composed of them.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of the wound is such that the patient plunges their hand into hot water until the flesh turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound slightly, so that the vein appears well, then it should be pierced crosswise, neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make a large incision, and pierce the vein near the joint of the hand, if it cannot be pierced, replace the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	if it is cold, do not immerse the hand in hot water, because it puts more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the right hand's saphenous vein is good for all liver diseases, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	hold the hand and push into hot water until the vein is empty, if you can see it.
