et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the wound is transverse, and you cover it completely, it will cause no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep for nerves are all beneath devoid of flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then place the hand in hot water, if the wound is frozen and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as is necessary, place oil and wax over the vein to solder it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand applies to the sickness of the mice, and do the same as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The salve of the soffion [a type of poultice] applies to all diseases under the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as diseases of the mouth, retention of flowers, diseases of the anus and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient should dip their foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it fades away.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And lay on top of the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot it goes very deep.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Cut open the deepest artery or at the ankle, for that is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below and make a cut as in skinning; let the flames be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the wound cannot be opened, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to drain the first time, the second follows shortly afterwards above a little, for the flesh is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerve, as we have said, and do so with the tendon of the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic nerve is at the knee, and its draining relieves the pain of the thigh, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of his health are such that the patient submerges himself in water and pulls up the calf four times while twisting it.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, you should treat it in all ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to cut it, for the limb is sausage-like, and it responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not release it, no remedy will open or close the small hole of the foot, and beware of nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make such a cure for the blood as you see fit, then release the ligament, put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Ventouse cures
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or hairs, or glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cautery called "ventosation" is performed in two ways: either it is to be used on all fires, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this cautery called "ventosation" performed by cutting and bleeding is made in twelve parts of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one is completely within the head, and others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck; and the ventous under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the boils on the two shoulders; and the boils on the ankles;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the boils in both arms; and the boils on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the boils on the two ankles; and the boil-formation does not deal with blood, unless it is small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore do not open them like you would when treating blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	It should not be administered (aministree) in any way, neither with fire nor burning fire, in any disease that comes from swelling, until the entire body is emptied (vuidiez).
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If it is necessary for diseases to be bled, or due to custom, then we shall administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle as well as at any time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if those who find repletion and redness in their face, head, and neck become dark-eyed;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a spot of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has swollen, and they bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who think, see by night blood and swell and die and similar things;
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during winter months, we instruct to fumigate after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The swelling of the mouth helps with the throat pain ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the entire body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this fumigation is in place of the swelling of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not appropriate for those of cold complexion to use [the treatment] or who have scurvy, for it does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently heal themselves become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the leech a little lower out of fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The leech in the neck is located at the site of the head and the basilica, and therefore it has value for the treatment of the feet.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And to cut through the channel of the pommel, and at once, and to fill it up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	It is necessary to push a little on it, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause distortion or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Wind in the two costals of the neck is worth as much pain as a headache, and otalgia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the position of the artery of the basilica; and you must command the lord to put his hand on it, so he does not hit the artery, and there should be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations beneath the chin are useful for diseases of the mouth and corruption of the gums, as well as similar illnesses that are within the mouth; and it is in the position of the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the sides are as effective as four veins in the arms.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And command the lord to not pierce too deeply, for the limb is bare of flesh, and knows beneath the dark and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The plaster that is on the buttocks is beneficial for treating piles from below, and for diseases beneath, and it must be large, made of flax, because it needs to draw well; and if it is fine, it would break; and this causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The plasters on the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are beneficial for old rain sores, scrofula, bladder diseases, and reduce the flowers; they are in the region of the hips and knees, and weaken the body after long use, and bring pus into various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the cupping glass is as follows: First, you empty it and fill it promptly, then apply it quickly and evenly, do not stop doing this until you see the spot turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then cauterize, and place the cups again, taking care in the positioning of the body, for there are some who have cold skin or clear pores: it is necessary to make a single incision, and it is necessary to make wide cuts, and a little deep one; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to make a third incision; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we must pierce it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to take much blood, we should often encourage [it]; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it fully, and we make sure that the arteries are severed suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, that you anoint the joints of the veins with stimulating and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from the seeds of cucumber:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in the ivy, oil of watercress, or lilies, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one whom you are healing has tender flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on it.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it must be washed after the ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of blackberries, or water of cucumbers, or water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise with ashes of sage or of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has large excesses should rise with old wine, or juice of vinegar, or decoction of dandelion or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he urinate when he should be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard if the one who is healed is colicky, and if the one without is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it must take cold things, such as green apples, endive, lettuce and similar;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat fresh meat, mutton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution, let him take syrup of honey, sweetened weak wine, which is between old and new, and consume little bread, and little pulses (beans, peas), and small birds and sparrows.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And the day he will vomit, let him drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give certain men sometimes tricolor or muscat wine before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the wine be refined, but it is not suitable for those who drink warm [liquids].
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The blisters placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, on the spleen, on gout, and on the stomach, the belly, the flanks, and the hips, because these limbs cannot bear to be wounded there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one should not use it except to draw blood from one member into another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	As we place on the breasts when the nails swell; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place leeches on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, remove by its attractive power accidentally the obstruction, or dislodge the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way it is done when placed upon the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are applied empty for suction only; sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in cases of pleurisy and such, and in this manner the blister is filled with hot water or with water boiled with herbs convenient for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two deep holes of about one and a half palms wide and long, and it should have one small hole around the middle, as when pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and made of ivory, soft before so that it does not cut the patient while placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have a rod of iron or steel passing through its middle to insert a handle.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For, the varicose veins of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones from thick ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this varicose vein should be placed thus upon the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a candle or thread and place it across the vein that is within the varicose vein.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	So that the light is at the bottom of the bladder (ventouse) so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, your fingers on the opening that we mentioned earlier, so that when you see, if steam comes out, remove the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Wrap it in linen as before and reapply it often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder given in disease of pleurisy (pluresin), there is neither a pipe nor an opening, and it is not administered except when it is full of liquid, and is placed only on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its shape: [This line does not contain any words that need to be translated, as "shape" (forme) is a direct translation of "forme".]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Snauses are not applied except in members where no bladders can be placed due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the naked parts of the skin, such as palms or soles, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and when the user finds snauses that are in sweet clear waters without purification, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them in a warm soft egg, until they are familiarized, and have nothing inside their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then it should be drained of veins and blood vessels, then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply a plaster on top.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are swollen and warm, if it is a place where blood vessels can be placed, then place a leech there, for that works very well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the wound from the dressing and clean it with warm water, then sprinkle it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the joint becomes too warm after the body, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on top until the swelling is reduced;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the swelling increases, apply broken glass or similar substances on top until it is reduced;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put half-peeled beans on the joint and leave them until they stick to it, then it will be reduced now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other swellings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the place of fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the vein bursts.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then lay them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle a little of aloe powder and crushed linen or ash on top, they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Understand, dear child, that the foolish person casts this chapter aside, who has never seen any old books, nor have they read letters from it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, knowledge in our land is foreign, since I never found any good of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have dealt with it in my practice, and through experimentation, and the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are brought, just as I have done in these 2 chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the prologue of this book, the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a breakage or dislocation or twisting or quassure comes to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to treat the patient on both sides, if anything does not prevent you from doing so, such as frailty of body, infants, or old people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the time is not very hot or too cold; and eat cold meats, namely cold joints of meat, poultry, and mutton, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill oneself too much with foods that fill veins with blood, before you have doubt about abscess heating or spreading of matter in the limb; then the patient will return to a better state of health as he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make thickenings, or he should have viscosity, such as cooked oats in water, and meat pies, and pork, and veal, and beef, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment helps the bones to heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones from the elderly and the weak cannot be well restored nor joined according to their nature due to the lack of strength in the limbs, neither those who are too tender, such as a child's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone on top of it (gross tenons which splint and join the limb together), as much as possible in the same way as before; and not to move it at all, and for this reason feed him with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks (injuries) are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is other than the break of the foot, or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is a break that heals quickly, and another that lengthens, like the quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with an open wound, or just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its instrument and proper tool for restoration, according to what the memory brings in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the fracture of the bone is caused by this: the joint is twisted, widely opened through displacement, and sounds when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can indeed have twisting, a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but put on the following medicines and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go to the tree (or joints), and they are the two parts disjoined, you must now put them equally back together, otherwise abscesses will grow there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come there, let it last for any day, as long as the abscess is healed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it equally in the muscles that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are fragments; then bind it, as appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces and divided into two parts, whether it be of the hand or foot, or at your hand if it is of small members, or at the wrist or arm, or at the elbow and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you must reset all the joints in their places with every means possible at your disposal, and ensure that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	align well the two bones' heads according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not good; straighten it carefully, and do not strain it too much, nor force it as those who make abscesses or contractions in the member through their work do, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is set, punish the patient so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch carefully that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	Because when it feels no pain, it is not broken, it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight so that twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are various in smallness and in largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members such as arms and fingers: you should wrap them with soft and thin linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: you should wrap them with a wide and strong rope, for the thick ropes embrace the entire large member and tighten it uniformly from all sides, so there is no pain.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light bandages around it four times or five according to the member, and tighten your hand a little on the rope, then go above the fracture and tighten less than the fracture, then move away from the fracture a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy limb, then take another ligament and turn it around in reverse on the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part under the break, and pull it gently, neither too strong nor too loosely, as we said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the ligaments with linen or cloth strips until they are all equal, then tie it all up above with one bandage, and then place your splints well made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or boil, place warm soothing material on it and let the boil remain for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind your limbs with a half-thickness large bandage or splint made from the wood used for clefts, or with palm reeds, and they should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the bandage placed on the fracture be slightly larger and thicker than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as is required for the limb, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	hold it steady on the stretcher in the same way as you did at the first joint, then tie it up with thread coming from above, as in the first joint when breaking.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the string should be tighter, closer; and it should be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and of flax thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	If the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of foolish people who make their cords from twisted linen and it is a great error; for the cords cannot be even if they are too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is impaled by the points of the splinters after setting a fracture in healthy bones, put linen or canvas padding under them so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with breaking and the ligaments are torn, I will tell the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set a splint for all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For large limbs, it is not necessary to apply splints immediately but rather after 5 or 7 days or more, according to the certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of old emplasters for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: it is to take flour that is kept near the mill walls and mix it with a lot of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and it is the common method for emplaster healing fractures in various ways, and equally for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractures, dislocations and twists: take alum, radish juice, sulfur, asafetida and Arabic gum, mix .x. parts; add mastic and aloes, .v. parts; eight parts of camphor; then make powder, and mix it with egg yolk; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of making a plaster for twisting: take mastic and amber, mix .x. parts; add mastic and aloes, .viiij. parts; vi. parts of camphor; Armenian pitch .x. parts, grind well, and mix with vinegar or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of making a plaster for disjointed joints and displaced bones, to relieve the pain occurring and cut the bone, heal the fracture: take new linen, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it on the affected area. This plaster does not heal, but it is good for relieving hot abscesses and proper treatment of pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground up earth-parsley, mix them together and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of plaster to aid in the healing of a wound caused by an arrow and for treating an abscess. Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, bean flour, and mix them all together; boil with wine, and when the affected limbs are hot, use it with moist coriander water or vinegar.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way of plaster stronger than the first, for healing a hard abscess in the limb. Take roots of mallow, flax seeds, broom, clover and horehound, violet flowers and camomile, mix them all together; boil with salt water, sweet water, or wine according to the heat of the limb and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book not to put anything on a broken limb for restoration except wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he states that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that something dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, should be put on a broken limb for restoration, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat wounds and pain is: take crushed mugwort and hops, or feathers of birds, and mallow, and equal parts, grind them together, and make a poultice with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then the dislocation a little while later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not dislocate it by hand for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain or itching comes at the joint, with no rest, swelling, or inflammation, hurry and dislocate it immediately, remove the emplaster now; take a light cloth and sea sponge dampened, dip in water, and lift the joint until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen wet with water or rose oil on it, and bind above a hot compress until you are sure of the abscess being heated.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be removed, then start the treatment subtly, and a little plaster, and not to strain it too much as before; and treat it subtly until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, and painful, and you need plaster and linen, start it again as you did initially equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not remove it for 3, 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes let it stay for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the break heals, and the abscess approaches the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore hold it (the dislocated shoulder) more tightly than before, and increase its flesh as I said earlier; and if you see the joint dry out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then warm it with hot moist heat every time you dislocate it, and do so for three days, and slightly loosen the ligament.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Therefore, through this process cut off the nourishment to the limb and hasten the healing of that which the foolish surgeon leaves twisted: it is bad, and it is a dangerous treatment, and I see nothing but weakening and correcting it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	In various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many breakings are of various kinds, and various shapes, and the causes are determined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are breakings made by sword blows that fracture the bone completely from its base to the surface of the bone, as a chop or strike does; and this is called this type of breakage "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or if the sword strikes the bone from above and penetrates through, it is called this type of breakage "absolute"; and the wound caused by these two types of breaks can be either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep bruise or cut, or arrow wound, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the wound is deep enough to reach the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is hidden in the bone just as fine as a hair, and it is a small cut, for this reason it is called "hair-like" wound.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling, or by similar things, causing the bone piece to go inside, and the wound looks like an egg when potters make pots over fires; if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist bone heads, such as infant skulls;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens in all these ways of breakage that small pieces are displaced, as bones; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaks by pulling on them, and the examination by probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy appearance is known by those who, when the bone is exposed and rubbed on top, causes the break to open black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the patient's symptoms; if you see any bad symptoms such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paralysis, high fever, hairs emerging and reddening, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms, and you hope for salvation, start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the frostbite comes to you for the first time, in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the events that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must make an incision in the broken part: and it is to grasp the patient's head firmly, and uncover above the bone in all possible ways, and over the wound area as much as possible,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the wound exposes the bone or abscess bursts, help with whatever is necessary, and it is to fill the area with damp linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and the flow of blood is stopped; then start working around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two ways of treatment: one way is that you make a narrow cut in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And put another, larger incision next to the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is to have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with iron tools; work carefully so as not to pierce the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is dislocated and hard, you should perforate it around [the area], so that you can administer splints with wedges, not penetrating more than the bone near the tip, and above the point there should be a margin or circle that prevents the tip from passing beyond the bone; and you should have several of them, so that each one comes to the appropriate place on the bone's thickness, so that you have splints for all [the parts]; and this is the shape of the four types of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for perforating around the broken bone is that you place one splint on the bone, then turn your hand until you feel that the bone has been perforated; then move the splint elsewhere a little afterwards, and do this all around, then cut the space in the bone between the fractures as subtly and lightly as possible, and as delicately as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand, or any of the tools you have like pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have perforated and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the dislocation with an instrument resembling pliers, but it must be thinner and more delicate than regular pliers.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains anything of the small bones, no scales, gently remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Gauls say, who are very wise; and it is praised much, and these are its words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture moves open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath it this lenticular incisure (as shown in its form):
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and the parts are sharp on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly pierce the bone all around, and take care of the cloth that is beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, strike the bone lightly, for one strikes it too much and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the cloth and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then after that roughness, remove the scales with a sharp rasp, using different amounts according to each place, in order to bring about the most suitable smoothing, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king shaves with great razors, and afterwards with finer ones, and never ceases to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you apply the remedy according to his guidance; this is not something that can be answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, it is necessary that you take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and place it over the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth doubled in 2 or 4 layers, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this more gently so as not to irritate the wound, then administer another thread above it, but do not tighten it any further than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it [the abscess] remain for one day or two, until the abscesses calm down, then uncover and administer medicines like roots of lilies, flour of oats, incense powder, aristaologue, and similar things; from these things make a powder and put on the wound, and administer immediately medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	Make sure the wound remains always clean, you must not let any ointment or bandage remain there, for when bandages accumulate on the linen cloth of the brain, they rot and cause pain, and it causes great harm to the patient; for when something sharp is placed over it, it bites through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no bad accident befalls the patient as we have said, it is doubtful with uncertainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come violently except through medicine that has been applied, then you should take a part of honey and 3 parts of rose oil, mix it with one cloth piece, and apply it to the sore.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure in the manner of cures that is necessary, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck are broken above, or one alone, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and push the breakage equal to your index finger inside, and towards the bellybutton through the mouth, until the nose returns according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the breakage is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, then you must place it equal to the top of a ruler, a little larger.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, then you should set it again, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has cooled down, then apply a linen cloth to the head of the wound, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply a bandage on the other side, if there is only one fracture; and let the cloths be as thick as they fill the wound of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that you should moisten the cloths with butter and change it each day. It does not seem good to me, but it is better that they are moistened in an ointment made of egg yolk and flour; then leave the cloth, until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of geese are placed instead of stitches, and if one piece of cloth surrounds them, and the breakage is held, the patient is blown upon with breath; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If abscesses come to the wound while you are working on it, place either alum or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of turmeric.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If abscesses do not come to the wound, apply an ointment from outside, made of sisamend flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light compresses on it, but do not bind the wound.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the neck is small and it is broken into little pieces, take suitable instruments to remove it, then make an incision, and treat the wound with things healing such as fat, sinew, and bandages appropriate for that purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound within the neck, then treat it with linen and place woolen threads on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated beneath and there is no wound outside, and only the break is outside but not broken in two, if one knows it slightly, it indicates that it is corbeled inside.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jaw, insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left jaw, place your index finger of the right hand inside, and gently push the break inward and align it with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts (i.e., diastasis), you must provide two parts of extension until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or rupture, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken cork over the mandible, and put on one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large and well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and attach it where you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and encourage them to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then reset to its original state; place a plaster over it with flour from the mill mixed with egg or meal of wheat; after removing the cork; and put a light linen plaster over the plaster when it dries, and if the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess arises, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, observe that no piece of the bone has been removed; if it is necessary to remove the broken part, do so with subtle tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, stretch it by fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once all the pieces have been removed and none are left, stitch the wound if it is wide, and place one plaster suitable for this purpose on it to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is in four ways: it is fractured and dislocated in two, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is a fracture with an open wound, that you have two assistants: one holds the shoulder where the forceps are broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then align the fracture to your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither deformation nor dislocation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if more extension is needed, put a round cushion of cloth or linen under the shoulder of the patient, and make it as large as necessary; stretch and tie the bandage, and hold the cushion in place with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot draw out the head of the splint from below because it is lodged in place, then have the patient lie on his side, and put a small pillow under the shoulder. Then push the shoulder downwards, so that the bone of the splint is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the break to your fingers and if you find debris, then it should be cut open. If the pieces cannot join due to any reason, hit it at one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the splint, to prevent it from flying out.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it should seem like a spoon, not hollowed out, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the task at hand; and have two heads, as you see, and one of them wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you have made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the abscess's heat, if the opening is small or you doubt the abscess's heat, use linen and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the abscess becomes cold, moisten one linen cloth in rose oil, asafetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it has wounds and incisions, is to put the padding of mill powder and egg yolk on top of the bone, place light stoppers on it, and put a spear under it if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage of one palm's width, then put one double cloth cover on top of the stoppers, and apply the padding. Then take a subtle stick of three feet long and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, turn the bandage over the neck, and under the saddle of the healthy and diseased sides, and tighten it from each side. When you see that the fracture holds the breakage properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then keep it in place every day, and when the ligaments loosen, hold it tightly.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And make the patient lie on his back and place a small pillow under his shoulders to raise the shoulder; align the fracture of the joint with the alignment of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, until twenty days pass.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then begin the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and hold it in place until it is restored; and it is restored at most within 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
