Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated from its place, and one can only feel it by touching; if it appears according to the shape of the break, and you reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways; then put powder from the mill on top with a lot of egg white, light bandages, and put on .i. double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle needle, about one finger wider than the shoulder, and if there are any holes in the needle at any place of the shoulder, fill those holes with linen bandages so that the needle heals evenly; and then hold it tightly with a strong bandage, so that the needle does not move from its place, and watch the ligament every day; and whenever it softens, hold it again, and adjust the needle if it is out of its place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 30 days. And when this number is completed, release it, and be sure, for it is not easy to put the bone back lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a part of the bone protrudes before and not under the skin, lift it up, extract it, and do what we have said to treat an abscess at the shoulder joint with warm cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break in the thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The peas is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the tip. And when it is broken inside, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain, lack of strength, and immediately vomits blood. The fracture opens the cavities in the broken bones, and it hurts very much.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and you place one cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and carefully align it in all ways, until the figure of the bone is as required; then you place splints and padding over the thin part of the broken bone, or a lighter staff, and wrap it in one bandage, and hold it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it gradually, and check every hour whether the bandage has softened, if it has softened, you tighten it; and if it is necessary to unwrap, due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and undo it, remove the padding, and direct those who have come in matters of care; then rewrap the padding, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs occurs only in large ones after the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend easily except because they are slippery; and this is well known at the investigation of the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture back in place as required. Then put a plaster on it and hold it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is displaced downwards, the patient feels very great pain and swelling, as in pleurisy, because the bone points to the skin; and it swells at the ends, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have applied many devices.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And to those who say that it is necessary to administer foods which swell the belly, for pushing out the rupture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	But we do not do so, that hot abscesses come, if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, he is cured.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it was said to someone that vents (tubes) should be placed on the head, for draining pus, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the tubes will attract excess fluid to the head due to its weak position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And it was said to someone that the head should be covered with damp linen in hot oil, and tents (something like small bags or pouches) should be placed between the ribs to make the wound even around it, then let it be treated with a cure for pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient experiences great pain that he cannot bear due to the broken bone not allowing cloth, there is doubt for the patient; then it is necessary to cut above the head of the broken rib, and a splint should be placed underneath. Then you should saw through the bone, extract gently, and sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and let it heal with plasters until it is healed. And if an abscess comes out, then place moistened linen soaked in rose oil on top of it; and treat the head of the abscess as necessary while lying down on the side where it is located, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a fracture occur in the bones of the neck or spine, and it rarely bends.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when it happens and you want to know if it will heal or not, if you see its hands softened and swollen and dead, and it cannot move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, it does not feel pain. Know that it is mortal in various positions, and if it is silent and feels good when stretched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if one applies treatment to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when something similar happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if there are injuries in the hands, and the back arches involuntarily; and when it is pressed on the stomach, it jumps involuntarily. And when it is pushed down on its back and wants to sit, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is to apply hot poultice if there is an abscess, then put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is soothed; then put one of the comforting and drying plasters on top and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, it should be covered with oil; extract the bone, then sew together two lips of the wound if it is large, with a stitch; then treat the wound with soothing balm until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken (which is called "head of the cow"), put your hand on it from the left side, and align it with the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the linen cloth on top, if you need them; then bind it, and if there is any bone dislocated, make it straight, extract it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the pelvis
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the pelvic bone is fractured, there will be a slight decrease in the head, and it will elongate and bend towards the opening, causing pain at the site, and swelling of what is fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, as long as you are over the fracture; and feel which part is fractured and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then make the fracture equal, as natural.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it bends towards the inside, then make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place the splint upon it, then place a rod or stick on top and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and immerse the limb beneath the ribs until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has come to the surface, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and place what we have said before on top of it; then return to treatment, hold it as necessary, if there is no bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the chest and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways; of which one is that you take a splint made of thicker material, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two ropes, and bind them from above, and place the patient on one seat; then you cast the broken arm upon the splint, until it reaches the elbow, and have a protrusion of splint in the middle, then bind it above to any heavy object or the assistants extend it downward; then the healer equalizes the fracture with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another manner is that you hold the patient on their bed, and hold their hand to their neck, then command two servants that one holds the place above the break with his hands, and the other holds below at every joint, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the extraction is stronger, hold one joint below the break and one above the break, and each servant extends to its part. If the break is near the shoulder head, you must put a moderate joint below the neck and another towards the back, below the break; if the break is towards the back, you must slightly tighten it without strain, so that the break is level with the neck and the shoulder; then adjust the break as necessary, but keep it tight, unless an abscess swells.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess swells up, do not tighten it for more than 7 days, but put soft linen and rose oil on it to calm the abscess; then you can tighten it. The method of tightening is that you place the clamp on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; then pull the cloth tight on the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its socket, unless something prevents it, or the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stitches; place a larger and stronger splint above the break, with one inch of space between each stitch, and make sure each stitch is large enough to pass over the break from both sides; then hold the splint in place as I have said at the beginning of the chapter concerning the break, more tightly and lessen in width.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the position of the splint and the tension, as we have said, during the time when you set the broken limb, and you doubt that it is healing well, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then examine every three days the sutures, to ensure that inflammation does not appear or swelling comes to the place, or new growth does not come to the limb because it is too tight. Follow our advice.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accident occurs, do not remove it for less than four days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; place one compress of equal wool under the shoulder, and examine every hour of the day or night to ensure that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the sutures are not softened; follow our advice through the power of medicine, and give them the food we have previously mentioned, so that the food is initially subtle; and when it begins to heal, let it be thick. It is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset in forty days, and then you should remove it and administer baths and ointments to guide the healing. If the incision is ugly and swollen, wait one day or two months before removing it.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius," the former being small and forming the forearm's outer side, while the latter is larger and lies beneath it near the elbow; by chance, only the large ulna breaks, or both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the small ulna bone is broken, the repairing and healing are easy; but when the large one breaks, the healing is poor, and more difficult than when both break together. If it's the small ulna that breaks alone, you should stretch it slightly and straighten it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large ulna that breaks, you should apply more force; stretch it up one cubit and elevate the wrist of the hand higher than the others, while keeping the smaller bone lower than the others; have the patient cross themselves on their chest, with a cubit in front of them higher than their chest, so that the patient doesn't feel any pain; then extend the attendant's arm below to the patient's side or elbow, and another attendant above. And then align the bones according to their best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage of bones, place each one back in its place, and if none is displaced that points to the center, and you cannot restore it to its place, then saw off and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking open, I spoke of it in the singular chapter, take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of healing, abscesses occur frequently, then apply a bandage made from oil and white beeswax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and stick one bandage above it subtly until the abscesses have subsided. Then remove the beeswax, and put the plaster of flour powder with egg on it, then place the splints, and the splint for the break should be more prominent than the others, and a little larger; and know that it must have 7 or 9 splints in various positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; and hold the break higher than the other parts, and always less on the sides, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages above the break be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the threads, which are used for binding, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And check the member and the ligament afterwards after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents come to a member, such as pruritis that comes to the member, you must irrigate the member with hot water until the itch is appeased; and do not allow the member to rest afterwards. Then proceed with the setting, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, give advice accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, you must soften it a little, and let it be for some days until the swelling subsides, and then set it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not remove the splint for up to twenty days. Or inquire about it after ten days, and place his hands at his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in thirty or forty days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture of the hand occurs frequently in the back of the hand and the fingers, but only a few breaks occur at the wrist.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or fractured, the patient must cross their arms and sit upright in a straight position; then place their hand on an extended cloth, and extend the broken bones, aligning them with mirrors until they are well set; apply the plaster and bandages, unless abscesses appear, then put a splint according to the size of the break; and swaddle it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is around the palm near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to wrap it around their broken hand; then tie it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as wide as the palm of the hand, and tighten it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outer side (of the bone), it is necessary that you place a splint above and another below in the sole, so that the hand remains open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and compress the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break occurs in any of the fingers, equal it as necessary; and hold it with the sole and, if you see, place a small straight splint to lift the break and keep it from moving; and if the break is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, equalize it, and tie it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together in one holding, for movement is harmful, or place a splint on it, as with a finger; and take care in the restoration and the placement of the abscess, and treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when it twists forward and backward; and restoration is such that a ligament is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their faces, then each of the ministers extends his ligament equally to its equal part; and this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one ligament should be towards the knee, and other ligaments below the break. And similarly, if it is near the knee, then the ligaments should be towards the knee, and the extension downwards; then set the bone equal to its two hands, according to its natural figure, and then put the plaster and stitch, except for abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the ligation is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should place a bandage of strong material doubled over twice or thrice and let the excess hang, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put one long stick between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the other end of the stick to the top; then turn the leg and the bandage above it, then tie the bandage to the break and tie a splint on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth between the leg and the thigh to make the compression equal, then start tying four or five turns around the break; and as you go higher on the break and tighten less; then take the two stitches that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then go below to the top of the stick, tighten so it does not move from its place, then let it stay, then there should be no abscess or swelling nor any similar problem.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a fracture, loosen it and direct the pieces as we have said many times; and if there are bone fragments that protrude, they must be removed if possible; and if not, the fracture should be opened and drained; and treat it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the leg is broken in such a way that stakes are set, as in the shoulder or arm; however, during the restoration process, the patient does not feel any pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the leg is restored in about a day, or slightly less or slightly more, according to the various complexions [of people].
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of genoails
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breakage, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is not just a crack or a puncture, but rather an opening, or a wound, which affects all the flesh and causes pain everywhere, and this is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one equalizes what is uneven in its ends, as much as it can be assembled; then place the splint, and put a round stick if needed, and tighten it as required, then inspect all the dispositions that we have said about other breaks, such as abscesses and others; apply to each accident what is necessary for it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called correctly "ham" (or shinbone), and the others are called "fibula"; and it happens a breakage similar to that which comes in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the procedure is the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg twists in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone (tibia) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it turns sideways. Then you must apply extension, make it even, and align the joints equally; however, if the fracture is misaligned and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two splints of wood that will support the leg from both sides and be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them with two bands, one above and one below, and bind it in the middle so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and this is good; nor should anyone apply a splint of wood longer than the length of the leg, and place it under the leg as a restraint for movement, and properly make it at the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fractures in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but sometimes the bones of the foot do have a fracture and nothing else except for a slight crack in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see the bones overlapping each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if he were walking, then place your own foot over his, where the raised bones are, press hard until they return to their place; put splints and bandages on, and put a small flat table under the patient's foot with two hollow holes, then tighten it around the foot evenly; when you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when four or five days have passed, undo the linen, for you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [shoulders] are broken, restore them as we have said about the arms of the hand; then place a splint on the broken shoulder according to its length and let it be slightly larger, then place beneath the arm that tabula I mentioned, and hold it in position; and if there are 2 or more [broken], break each one separately, place a splint on each according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the tabula beneath the arm; and let it be so that the tabula is placed above the belly of the arm, facing towards the back, so it covers well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, after what we have said; and treat each accident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the natural womb is broken, make her sit raised, then incline her to the part of the back and hold her from behind; then fill the hollow of nature with cotton, and put as much as one stone in it; then turn the woman, lean the back slightly and lift the buttock bit by bit, then jump the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the break will be restored. If you see, take a bladder of nettles, and attach a spout to it, and push the entire bladder into the nature; then blow strongly into the spout until the bladder is inflated inside: the break will return; then fill with cotton, and leave it for some days, until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the fracture of the pelvis; and these breaks should not be concealed from him who applies his study and skill to them and reads my book. For fractures indicate in many ways the right path of restoration: therefore, attend to this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a spear (shaft), when it is broken, take an owl's throat and insert the shaft; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for 3 or more days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For the one who has a breakage with a wound (especially if it is large such as the bones of the leg or shoulder), he must be bandaged now, just as the bandages that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then treat it with vinegar (if you have nothing else), then immediately proceed to set the breakage in that same hour or the following day, unless an abscess has come forth.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess has come forth, then wait until the ninth day, allowing it to heal before touching or working on it again, for doing so would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears above the knee joint, you must put it back gently into its place with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the fractured bone does not align to put it back into place, you must use this tool which is made of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and the width according to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary for the mirror that he grips 3 or 4, depending on what is needed in each bone-setting; and it should be round and a bit large, so that it does not bend during your work on the limb, and pointed at the tip, and large from the middle forward, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palancha", so the curved bones should be placed on the top of the visible bone; and push it once until it returns to its original position and is level with each other. If the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the top of the bone until the instrument has control over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do as much as you can to put it in its place, then moisten a small linen cloth in black stiptic vinegar, and carefully if it is in summer; do not put any ointment or other substance on the wound where there is oil, which may cause decay and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, and cover the entire area, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with a fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing death or rotting of some kind; and may the bindings be softer and more supple than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is bad or large and you fear that it may become infected, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, do not put splints on it; instead wrap around it, in place of splints, hard cloths, and bind it. And after one or two days, if you see swelling at the wound, remove whatever you placed there and apply healing ointments for wounds, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, as long as it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be set in such a way that the bone slips slightly downwards easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but slides back, as there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you try to keep pressure on the wound and remove all the loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If a fistula or other form of corruption occurs, it is necessary to treat it, as described in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open over a limb, like the bones of the leg or shoulder, and similar large members, do not draw it out, for many times death may come; however, leave it as long as possible; perhaps it will heal itself after twenty days or thirty; then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises on the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is unpleasant to see the appearance of the limb member; and by chance, the limbs cannot perform their natural duties.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be careful: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, such that you take any of these things or all together, and crush them with a sharp wine or with plenty of egg white or with oil; then put it on the wound in poultices, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days; and then break it open, and start another one, as long as the nodules are removed; or you bind above a piece of plank well made; because the properties of plank are that they remove all swellings from the limbs. And if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut off the top, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it at any razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The member which is weak after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after treatment, the members are weak and delicate in many cases: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many sutures, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or because of excessive drainage; or because of excessive movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, which makes them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body thin, until the blood multiplies in him; and administer baths, and give him joy and comfort; then put wax on the member, so that the wax attracts great nourishment to it, and drain it often with cold water, until the nourishment goes to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless do not lose hope; do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this treatment is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the swelling and torment are fresh, it is necessary that they be treated with hot, soft water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, radishes, mellilot root, and similar things; and you make a soothing poultice, such as dyaquilon; or you take figs with fat, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constantly and repeatedly rubbing it with wet hands. Movements should be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is swollen and hardened, just like stone, and it requires iron to be removed, then it must be covered up to the bone, incised carefully with a subtle instrument; and cloth and bandage should be applied in treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must now be returned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	If one waits, the joint swells, and perhaps it can be reset to its place; therefore, it should not be moved until the swelling has subsided; many times it causes pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Therefore, when this happens, first have the patient cleanse himself, then leave him to rest until the abscess subsides; then immerse the member in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and treat each member according to its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning shoulder dislocations down to feet.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that jawbones should be dislocated in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened somewhat; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and saliva flows from the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, wrapping its tongue around with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When small dislocations occur, they return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it immediately, do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner as the minister holds the head of the patient and pushes one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other hand should be placed aside to provide balance; and command the patient to relax, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he shall bring it back into its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it [the dislocation] is reduced with force, most certainly it will recur, especially if they are the two jawbones together, anoint them with hot water and oil, until they are gently reset; never force to reduce it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they [the jawbones] are gently reduced and the mouth of the patient closes well, cover it with a moist cloth made from rose oil and beeswax, then secure it lightly with several strips of linen.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	Let the patient sleep on his back, and his head be positioned between two pillows so it does not move to either side or make an effort, but take light food until the pain is alleviated, and let the jawbones heal.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then let him eat lightly, and he should not labor at all in opening the mouth to eat or drink, until the mandible is well swollen and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and accustomed sores come, and possibly rupture of the belly, and possibly the vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster; and many times he who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the noose
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The noose cannot dislocate from within its continuity and the ribs, and it is occasionally dislocated outwardly, and one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back and stretches out his arms; then presses the joint forcefully with your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage over it, and hold.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the joint which is facing the chest cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it occasionally dislocates, you reset it to its place as we have said; then place the splint and bandage over it, hold it, and command the patient to rest until he recovers.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, the head of the shoulder is returned to its place when it is dislocated from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder dislocates in only four ways: one is when it dislocates at the socket below; and the second is at the hip part; and by chance, it may dislocate above, but this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind the shoulder blade nor inside by the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those with little fat, because it can jump out quickly; in those with enough fat, it jumps out rarely and returns quickly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, percussion or breaking, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify [the dislocation], as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it is turned towards the inside [of the joint], and you find a clear difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder and under the inside at the top of the shoulder, as if it were an eye socket. The patient cannot return their hand to its place or make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it should not be hidden, because you can clearly feel it with your hand.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	This method of dislocation is not only to return it when it is new, but also when the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the minister raises the patient's hand up, then puts his thumbs under the dislocated joint and pushes it upward to its place; the minister then lowers the hand and places it down, it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said in normal hours after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water. And bring them a soothing and calming ointment such as the decoction of elder and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and bring it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should lie on his back and place a piece of even-sized cloth beneath the affected area, neither too soft nor too hard, then the person in charge should place their heel on the cloth and lift the head of the shoulder properly, pulling the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another assistant holds the head of the patient so it does not move downwards; that shoulder immediately returns to its place, and if you see it dislocate again in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you have a man who is larger than the patient present; and he should be facing towards the side, and push the shoulder of the patient under its joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister draws the hand of the patient towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, they can hold something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	You may also reset it in another way: and this is when you insert a long needle into the earth, with the head of the shoulder being as round as a pea, and neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then he should be placed under the patient, but with soft cushions beneath, and the patient lying on their back on a long bed. Then stretch out his hand away from the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not want to return due to all these things that we have said, perform this treatment: take one tison of two arms length and four fingers width, which has a round tip to enter deeply under the ascle (or shoulder joint), according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod over the patient's shoulder, so that it does not prick the patient; then place it under the shoulder of the patient; extend your arm along the rod; hold the limb on the rod and the arm at the wrist, then place the arm on one side of a small bench with enough space for the hands to be placed underneath; extend the other hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side; the joint will re-align itself in the process.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	When the joint is in place, regardless of how it may be, you must place a spherical pad of wool under the shoulder; then apply the plaster made with powder from the mill, incense, and egg white over the entire shoulder and around it; then press down on the shoulder underneath while turning the string around the plaster, and tie the hand to its neck, keeping the hands in place.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be applied ointment, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal sooner; and afterwards apply more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is moved out of place due to moisture which has come or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries to it three times, as mentioned in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm above, then know that the nerve at the base of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the thighs and hips, or backside, is made by a push and extension of hands, and other force is applied to it; and care should be taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes stiffness in the member and delayed movement; the patient should use baths many times, until the stiffness subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to its points; and if it has dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and dislocation cannot be restored because it can clearly be seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the ill shoulder with the healthy one, if you can clearly see it. For the joint is separated, and cannot bend the arm, nor can it touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the dislocation as soon as an abscess comes, for if an abscess comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely set again, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be returned in this manner, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands of the patient according to the cut thereabout, both above and below, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when the patient doubles their hand over their hand, and pushes the root of the displaced palm back into place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, then apply strong extension.
