It is that two people should extend the arm, and each of them should hold it still during the extension; then turn the arm from both sides, then wrap a doubled long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the doctor joins the joint to his hand, he should oil it to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, he should put on a plaster made of flour with egg, and pull it back into shape, and tie the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; if you see that the joint does not bind well, renew the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like that for some days until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels pain after the repositioning of the joint and it becomes stiff, bathe and rub it well and press until it is relieved; or you place a sheep's fat pad on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let it enter water again.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it bleeds, rub the joint gently, then replace the fat pad on it, and then let it enter water again; and do so two or three times until it is healed; if you see, place warm moist sheep's wool covered with butter and press it on; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is displaced and the repositioning is easy, more so than other joints; it should be returned to its place as quickly as possible, in the hour itself when it is dislocated, unless the ligaments are inflamed or there is an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the repositioning is that you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and place the mirror so it is level, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and pushes it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Moreover, it is necessary that you watch if it is properly in place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's hand dorsal side on the table, and have the patient place their other hand above the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, that's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	And if not, squeeze with plasters to ease the abscesses, and let them remain as they are until they begin to heal.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	If it cannot endure it and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the dislocated joint remains.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And the patient should not refuse fire until his hand is healed, and it cannot be strained by any means altogether: therefore understand that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is no other device for healing except to strain by fire cautery in this case, and by chance nothing else is of value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is healed, place it in a splint as we have said, then strap and leave for 5 days, then release and leave it in this state.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well and there is no swelling, moist with warm water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on one side, sometimes at the back or palm.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then, the finger is straightened, and you push the dislocation towards your fingertips until it returns, then hold the finger's head, and turn it towards the side where it is dislocated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And let it rest for 2 days, and then make it even on the third day; and bind it tightly, as we have said, and release it from time to time, and move it around, and rebind it tightly; do this often until it becomes narrow.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And the same applies if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before until it heals, and the same applies when it is dislocated from another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the vertebrae in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no remedy, for death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that excrement passes involuntarily, it cannot be held, and multiple limbs are weakened, such as the two legs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And multiple times the vertebra becomes paralyzed in four parts; that which becomes paralyzed at the rear is called "gibbotization".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The physician should observe whether the swelling has arisen from childhood; if there is no remedy or healing for it in its entirety.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old methods of cure used to speak in grand words, where there was not much benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling which comes before, there is no remedy nor healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also that which comes directly between two sides, can only be cured by the one who comes from behind, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And that the patient should be extended on one side, and have pressure underneath him so he does not bruise himself;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert one thorn into the head in the earth and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the patient's buttocks, and another at his hips, thighs, knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers know the ligaments, one at the head and others at the feet, among the four tendons;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be tightly closed, the tendons as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine forming, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return through this cure, take a board four feet long and shaped at the end, and place the patient on the side, and push the head of the board under the side, then put the middle of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and place the mirrors feet on the other head of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the turning tool that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you insert two needles into the patient's head, one in each arm of good size, and between each needle, outside and inside, a palm's space in length;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and in each needle have a pin or turnscrew, so that the needles do not move, and between two needles have one turning needle, like cords twist, and in the two twisting needles have two small pins of a palm's length, to twist the turnscrew;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is between the seated needles to the turnscrew towards the head, and another cord towards the other turnscrew, and each of the attendants twists his turnscrew along the entire cord, and the master equalizes the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a desiccating plaster on top with abundant egg, then pound it, then hold the head of a board of 3 feet long against the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it up with a rope, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nursing until he recovers;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	If anything comes at the end of his health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the stick as we have said before; sometimes they also administer a piece of wood.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes the appearance comes at the back of the spine near the spondile, and it is thought to be dislocation; but it is the bone that opens up, so one must not have any presumption: perhaps death may come as a result.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the shoulder and shoulder blade joints come from dislocations only, and they are not dislocated in the same way as other joints; the shoulder joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back, more inside than out, less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when the sick leg is joined with the sound one, it is longer, and the sick knee joints are more open than those of the healthy ones, and the sick one cannot bend his knee in the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the loosened joint filled with abscess pus, because that the knee joint comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is about to die, is that this event is contrary to those mentioned earlier.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one whose leg is straight according to the accomplishment, are that it does not double the knee due to pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he steps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one whose backside event occurs are that he cannot stretch his knee nor bend it, and the leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the thigh is in its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are as follows: first, you should examine whether the dislocation is old and if it stays in place according to its position, there should be no treatment; and there should be no presumption that it can heal on its own.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For the fresh dislocation, which is of the four kinds of dislocation, you should hurry and turn the joint, pushing it inward and outward, moving it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, there will be no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, then you must call for one strong man, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or tie him to the thigh;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another minister extends his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath the shoulder blades, then tightens a cord of rawhide around the thigh; and another holds the head with the cord.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And they all extend below at once, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If it is not dislocated, treatment for its similar condition is required. When the dislocation occurs at the shoulder joint, you should remind the patient to lie on their unaffected side, then place the rope around the thigh's root, and under the angle (shoulder), then draw the rope upward towards the angle and towards the armhole.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant with you and grasp the large thigh of the affected limb, stretch it out in an extended form; it will return to its place now; this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then tie the feet of the patient together tightly with a strong rope above their heels and knees, and extend the affected leg two feet more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then it should be hung by the head from a post, and it should be above the ground .ij. [two] long arms; then instruct one servant to embrace the thigh, and let another servant hang with the patient, who will then hold the thigh, for the joint is now returning quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the side [of the body], the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of a dislocated shoulder, and draw a rope over the affected leg properly, and above it also.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then place two ropes, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one rope between the thighs of the patient in the dislocated position;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And plant the damp cloths around [the area], so as not to prick the sick person, then extend each of the assistants toward him, and the mirror place equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, place it on a table and press as we have said in the swelling, and make the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended immediately as I have said, and place the mirror on the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the shoulder, it is not necessary to stretch the patient below, nor lift up on the earth, but rather he should be in the same position as when the hip was dislocated, as we have said about lying down on two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and he should be supine (on his back), and the limb extended as we have said before, and pressure should be applied on the joint to the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and will be at the right point when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and place the pillow under them, and hold with a bandage so that the hip does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And it rests for 3 or 4 days, then dislocate [the joint], and place a splint on it; and if you see that they are even, hold them steady as before, and let it rest. 3 days; then dislocate it, and make it move well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside and outward, behind; and do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee in your palms, pull apart between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee joint. Have another servant extend his foot until the knees return to their place, and the signs are that it bends slightly at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And apply the poultice on top, and tie the leg to the thigh tightly for 3 or 4 days, then release it; and let the patient rest, do not make them move at all until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the member is not broken, provide strong stretching as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes completely dislocated from within and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it bends towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is easy, and it should be gently extended to the hands when it is only crushed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit straight, and tie one minister (assistant) by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand two times, then lift it up, and push the foot up firmly;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this two times, as we have said, in pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the procedure, because it will return again;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return in such a way, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and firmly fix one peg tightly into the ground between his thighs, and tie strips around it so as not to prick the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the ministers should dye the thigh, and another minister should extend the leg to his hands or one link, so that he lies on top of the leg on the neck of the leg.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister should extend himself equally, and the peg should be close between the thighs of the patient to keep him when he is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the hands equally on the dislocation, and let another servant hold the healthy leg below; the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, apply the plaster and poultice on top, form the limb, tie it to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the calf, so that the bandage is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for 2 or 3 days and if the bandage becomes loose, tighten it; then unbind it on the third day or the fourth, and allow the patient to walk after 4 days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it goes before that point, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells there, you must soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they must be stretched out gently without strain, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back between the shoulder and the hip, you must make the patient sit. On a flat surface or table straight upright, put your foot on what opens these joints, then press your foot firmly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When it is even and does not open, put a table with two legs under the foot of your foot. Then press firmly and leave for three days, then release it. Let it rest until it heals.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	Do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and unless you are merciful and patient, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	Use at first soothing warm compresses for an abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place immediately, so that the abscess subsides.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limbs are at their place, administer soothing things to the abscess, and treat the wound, as necessary, with ointments that dry;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with dislocation there is a break, and small bones are displaced, set the bone, and do as we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for it is valuable to you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your weapon and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the medical book.
